<Author>bklyn274
<Content>Head Over Heels for Hix!!! A friend recommended Hix to my boyfriend as an awesome place for a chill and romantic vacation spot. Once we checked out the Hix website, we were convinced it would be amazing.Our expectations were far exceeded!! First of all, it's breath-taking and beautiful -- the landscape, the architecture, and the peaceful seclusion were just what we wanted. As soon as we arrived we said we would return.We stayed in Loft 1 which is HUGE and beautifully decorated!!! The table could seat 6 and there is a huge open window/ledge overlooking the pool. The outdoor shower is a spectacular addition. The bathroom also has double sinks and very nice Rusk shampoo/conditioner. The hanging bed is a wonderful spot to nap in the sun (and I believe that Loft 1 is the only loft to have one). Our actual bed was the most comfortable thing ever!We were only at Hix for two nights (we seriously considered extending our stay but a wedding party was coming in and we couldn't). Our two nights felt like much, much longer because it's just so relaxing. It's heavenly, really.The kitchen was fully stocked with pots, pans, cups, plates, silverware etc. The fruit/eggs/bread/coffee/juices in our fridge every day were so nice. We went to the Green Market shop to pick up a couple of other things, but otherwise had plenty of food provided for breakfast. We were also appreciative of the use of beach chairs, cooler bags, robes and towels they provided for us.As most other posts say, there are no screens on the doors/windows. We did not have any problems with bugs at all. (We were there in late June.) However, they do provide bug spray and candles if there are bugs and the mosquito net over the bed. You can also close the big window/garage door, if need-be.The pool is breathtaking -- there's a reason it's been voted the Best Pool in Vieques.Brenda, in reception, was wonderfully helpful both before and during our stay. She set up the Bio Bay tour tickets for us (which we highly recommend) and told us about the best restaurant in town - El Quenepo - where we had a delicious and romantic meal! Hi Brenda!Hix is hands-down the most amazing, relaxing spot we've ever been to. It's the perfect escape from the hustle and bustle of work etc. We will definitely return and couldn't recommend it higher!!!!

<Author>The_Dylaness
<Content>Not quite as expected I read nearly every review of Hix here on Tripadvisor, so I had a pretty good idea of what to expect. The reservation was easy to make and the staff helpful; we enjoyed Vieques and will return but not to Hix. I gave serious consideration to 3 stars vs 4 but ultimately decided on 3 given a few serious flaws and my feeling that the price is not in accordance with the product.The Good:The location is beautiful, peaceful, quiet, charming, birds chirping...The front desk staff are extraordinarily helpful and pleasant. The bread/fruit/butter/juice/coffee provided daily are a nice treat. The pool is lovely. The beds are very, very comfortable. Nice linens, nice robes, nice cotton shirts to wear during your stay are provided. Amazing views. The outdoor shower (we were in loft 5) is great. They have provided many things for your comfort and convenience, such as beach chairs, bug spray, candles, board games to check out, a book exchange library in each room, umbrellas to check out, a listing of local menus, et cetera.The Bad:I know Hix focuses on privacy, nature, and eco-friendliness. However, there are certain things that I personally expect when staying at a place that while not exorbitant, isn't exactly cheap either. I knew there was no maid service daily and so wasn't surprised (although I think for the price it should be provided- who wants to make their own bed on vacation?) The showers are heated by solar power and apparently also have a gas implement to bring the water to 120 degrees if it isn't already. This feature did not seem to work very well (intermittently) and at its hottest still was not hot enough for myself or my husband (who usually prefers much cooler showers than me...) The other disturbing problem was our toilet. It was a nice, fairly new toilet (Kohler I think?) with a very old, raggedy, stained plastic seat and lid combination that loooked like it had been brought in from an airport bathroom. I don't know why but the whole toilet smelled very badly of urine (sometimes you could even get a whiff as you walked right outside the bathroom) and was very unpleasant. I did mention this to the manager after the first night who immediately sent a very cheerful and hardworking housekeeper to remedy the situation. She scrubbed away and it smelled good...for about an hour. I had also mentioned the shower heating issue to him and he explained to me how to use the faucet a little better to get hotter water (which helped a little.) I guess my perception of hot water is perhaps different than most, so I didn't bring it up again but if you like really hot showers and it could be a dealbreaker for you, consider yourself warned. I also did not revisit the toilet issue because clearly her scrubbing although temporarily effective was not getting at whatever the issue was (I don't think it was her fault, I think it was something scrubbing wouldn't fix) and I was pretty sure it wasn't going to get resolved before we left. My husband mentioned that the seat would not stay up (as a female I have no idea about this) and this was also awkward for him.The neutral:I knew that a/c was unavailable but did think that it would get a bit cooler at night than it did. We did not sleep well. I also knew that there was not a jacuzzi so that was okay, but again, I am surprised that a place that bills itself as a fairly high end accomodation does not have one. Make sure to rent a Jeep if you're staying here (or anywhere in Vieques for that matter.)

<Author>Susanica
<Content>Hix is a great experience We stayed in Loft 1 in the Casa Rodonda in early July, 2008. We had peaceful time and I cannot complain about anything. Our view overlooked trees and the ocean in the distance. The only thing that obstructed our view was the numerous humming birds buzzing in and out the flowering tree that framed the huge open window. The outside shower was relaxing and it was gently laced with a green vine. Overall the room was spacious and clean. Surprisingly bugs were scarce. Basically Hix is a place to enjoy nature and relax. As far as Vieques, I recommend renting a 4 wheel drive and exploring the beaches and towns. Red Beach and Blue Beach were our favorites, but the more popular Sun Bay Beach was beautiful too. I recommend doing the bio bay tour, but make sure to check the moon phase first. The tour guides at Island Adventures were knowledgeable, funny and friendly. When exploring the towns be sure not to leave any valuables unattended. We had a set of snorkel gear stolen. Even with that one incident we felt very safe on Vieques and it was a great experience all around.

<Author>SPK_DK
<Content>Tranquility, peace and harmony As many have said previously, it's a fantastic place. It's very much a matter of taste, no doubt that Hix is not your standard hotel experience. So I understand why some may find it not to their liking, but if you have a proper understanding of what you're getting, then then disappointments shouldn't be an issue. I've tried to add some items which haven't been covered previously.We came from Hell to Heaven: after a 4-day conference in Fajardo, at El Conquistador, Hix stood out as phenomenal. We (a couple in our early 30's) we're getting nausious, depressed and fed up with the massiveness of El Conquistador, it's thousands of noisy guests, ringing and dinging Casino, and where just happy to get away from it. So Hix, being the exact opposite, was a true blessing.It's true that you will need a car. Book well in advance, as most places are fully booked fast. We ended up getting a car from Raphael at Acevedos Car Rental. A very decent Ford Explorer.The pictures from both the Hix website, as well as from the other reviewers give a good understanding of what it is, but as a lot of the Hix experience is tranquility, it's really hard to catch that in a still photo.The front desk is VERY helpful (we met Bob  Joanne), but don't forget to ask. They're not intrusive in trying to lure your wishes and desires, so just ask if there's anything you need, or something you need help on figuring out. Worst thing that can happen is a no.We stayed at Loft 5 for 3 nights, and then at Loft 1 for 2 nights. Loft 1 is quite a lot bigger, has two sinks in the bathroom, two sinks in the kitchen, a little desk, a hanging mattress by the patio, and in general is a lot more spacious than Loft 5. It's almost too big for two people. Loft 5 was nice, more simple but great as well. A simple square room with kitchen, bed and patio. Both great rooms. No problems with heat, the ceiling fan along with the outside breeze is quite perfect.I could only reach an internet signal while at the front desk, which actually was OK as it forced a bit more relaxation, and less work.We did a Eco Tour with Abes snorkling, doing the mangroves, snorkling, secluded beach and ending off with the Bio Bay. $100/person, lasting from 2 p.m. till approx 8 p.m. A great trip.El Quenepo is great for dinner.On Sundays the BBH serves an excellent brunch.There are two things would make the Hix experience better: firstly, a daily maid service, just to make the bed, clean the dishes etc. would be great. It's not a cheap place, so it wouldn't hurt with that little service. It's actually great and very much in tune with the whole atmosphere that there isn't roomservice etc. etc., but as the room can get messy after 2 or 3 days, it would be nice with a little bit of service. Secondly (and a very minor thing): a toaster in each room. There's fresh bread every day, but some of us like to toast it a bit, if for no other reason than for variation.

<Author>tornadodreams
<Content>Hix...I want to go back!! When we booked our 7 night stay at Hix House, I read most if not all of the reviews posted on this site. I was pleased to find them overwhelmingly positive, but admit I was a bit nervous about the 'oneness with nature' aspect, if you will. I am not a fan of bugs and spiders, despite being an outdoor person. So this review is for anyone with those same hesitations. Hix was the most relaxing vacation accommodation I have ever experienced, and it has set the standard for every vacation I will take hence. Sleeping under the mosquito nets turned out to be more of a rustic notion than a necessity. We didn't wake to a swarm of insects, as other reviews have suggested. In fact, I don't recall any at all on or near our bed, closet, etc. The occasional wayward beetle would find its way into the outdoor shower, but these were easily enough ushered out. As Leebc suggests, the lizards (curious but not intrusive) likely kept the insect population under control. I found myself embracing the natural surroundings and sloughing off the buildup of city and work stress, an aspect of true relaxation you wouldn't experience in a typical hotel setting. I reveled in going all week without makeup or blow-drying my hair, even to go out for dinner and drinks! The understated architecture blends beautifully with the serene environment, promoting an unspoken atmosphere of quiet and simply being. You suddenly feel less of a desire for music or television and prefer the sound of birdsong, coastal breezes, and the rare and almost unfamiliar quiet of your mind. I felt strangely indulgent in eating the fresh baked bread and fruit provided, despite it being so much healthier than typical vacation fare. You won't find Hix Island House conducive to a party vacation, although the nearby towns provide somewhat of an outlet for this if you desire it. We found that we rather preferred hanging out on the patio playing a game of Trivial Pursuit over several days, without keeping score. The staff was friendly, attentive, and helpful with everything from providing fresh beach towels when requested, to booking activities and making restaurant recommendations. (BBH completely validated one such recommendation, providing the promised 鈥渃hill South Beach vibe鈥?and gorgeous tapas and cocktail selection). Do not expect constant attention and catering to at Hix, however. The staff is there when you need them and otherwise give you your space and privacy. Our room was clean and well stocked from check in to check out, but we rarely bumped into housekeeping. There is so much more to praise about our stay at Hix, the perfect base camp for a week of exploring, relaxing, and soaking up the delightful eccentricities of Vieques. But it鈥檚 something you have to see for yourself and I don鈥檛 want to spoil it for anyone, not that you really could.

<Author>kristumz
<Content>Favorite hotel of all time We have stayed at the Hix House 3 times over the past 5 years, and it is a wonderful experience. Architecturally, it is beautiful. Conceptually, it is a great Caribbean experience.It is off the beaten track, quiet, secluded, surrounded by tropical flowers and trees. It is open-air (no glass or screens) with enormous panoramic picture window openings. There is a full kitchen in every room, and the staff brings you fresh breakfast supplies every morning (homemade bread, island fruit, fresh coffee for the French press, etc).You will love coming back here and making dinner with your travel partner after a long day exploring the beaches in a run-down jeep. The pool is surrounded by lemon trees and great for a late night swim. The roofless showers in the second floor rooms are amazing under the stars as well.The hotel is eco-friendly, doing things like watering the plants with greywater and using solar power to heat the showers, and does not allow children under 12. It is the perfect romantic escape. This is true to the point that we returned after two fantastic visits to have our wedding here.

<Author>giggy19
<Content>A different....but wonderful place My wife and I took a quick trip from New York to Vieques in May and stayed in the Hix House.In past trips to the Caribbean we had stayed mainly in very nice resorts like Caneel Bay in USVI, but this time we were looking for something less expensive, but still not like a big overblown resort. Hix Island House was just as described. It was peaceful, interesting, very in-tune with nature, etc. Within the first minutes of arrival we saw geekos and hummingbirds from our window (which is nothing like a real window!) We really enjoyed it despite its minimalist, very casual approach. Vieques too was fun and interesting. Great beaches with virtually no one else on them. Wild horses everywhere. Pretty decent restaurants (we ate twice at the Chez Shack and highly recommend the walk from the Hix House on a starry evening.) We enjoyed the Bio Bay -- it was a little touristy (as far as anything can be touristy in Vieques) but a fascinating natural wonder that we're unlikely to experience anywhere else.With the right expecations, Hix is a wonderful experience. Highly recommended!!! If you have the wrong idea of what it is, however, you might be sadly disappointed.

<Author>theLAgirls
<Content>Beautiful, quiet location Hix House is in a beautiful, quiet, remote location. The architecture was unique, especially for this part of the world, so no room is the same. The pool is beautiful and refreshing. As other reviews have pointed out, you cannot be afraid of nature to stay here. Our room had basically barn doors that stayed open all day, whether we were there or not. Obviously, this meant we had some visitors along the way - small lizards, bugs, spiders, even a cat that quickly ran away - but we loved it and were not afraid of any of this stuff. There is a mosquito net but we didn't need it this time of year. It is quite dark at night as the property and rooms are not well-lit. Frankly, it creeped me out a little at night with how dark, quiet and remote it is, but i live in LA so maybe it's just me. You will likely need a flashlight though - we needed it to find our car!We also loved having a kitchen and being able to cook. Every day we had fresh baked bread, juice, fruit, eggs, milk and coffee. It was all tasty and wonderful. The staff was very helpful.We did yoga one day and it was a good, albeit easy class, somehow we had thought it was free from the Hix website. In fact, it was $15/class which lasted about 1.5-2.0 hours.You will absolutely need a rental car. Nothing is nearby and getting to our parking place proved a little treacherous, as we had one of the many junky island rental cars with bald wheels.

<Author>MissyfromMichigan
<Content>Wonderful, relaxing place to stay! My husband and I stayed for 4 nights, in the beginning of March (a few weeks ago). We had a wonderful time!I'll admit that after reading some reviews, I was really concerned about bugs, lizards, etc, but I was really comfortable there. We saw very few bugs, and only a few very tiny lizards. The lizards stayed over near the patio and the entryway, and never came near the bed or closet areas, so they really were not a problem.The Hix Island House is very clean and extremely peaceful. There are no TVs, clocks, radios or internet access within the rooms, which is exactly what we wanted!The staff was very friendly and helpful. The women who worked at the front desk were both great - they gave us directions, recommendations, and helped us by booking a trip to the bio bay.The landscaping around the hotel grounds is gorgeous. We were on the ground level and had flowering bushes surrounding our patio. The hotel is inland, so the view of the ocean was extremely limited, but we still thought we had beautiful scenery.Staying here was a fabulous experience! Sleeping in the fresh air, with the sounds of the birds and the wind, was great! We woke one morning to rain, and loved it - the sound and smell of the rain was a great way to wake up!I would suggest buying groceries and planning to eat in the room for several of your meals (there's a full kitchen). There is only one restaurant that is very nearby, but it was closed when we tried to go there (which was around 5:00 on a weeknight, so they must have irregular hours). The hotel is about a 10-minute drive from the nearest town, which isn't a bad drive but it did become a little tedious when we had to make the drive multiple times each day.One more suggestion is to try to arrive before 5:00 pm. We arrived after dark. We had been told that the office would be closed. As promised, there was an envelope waiting for us, with our name on it, with the key to the room and directions for getting from the office to the room (the office is in a separate building from the 3 buildings that house the rooms). Being completely unfamiliar with the area, we were a little confused by the directions. We did make it to our room (after starting out in the wrong direction, plus I was nervous, thinking I was going to run into a lizard as I was walking around the side of the building to our room), so the directions were correct, but it would have been easier to find our way during the day.I would definitely stay here again!

<Content>fabulous, tranquil, relaxing Most beautiful setting on vieques, super comfortable accommodations, and very efficient little kitchen. <Author>getaway9
<Content>Astonishing property Hix Island House byFrequent Caribbean TravelersWe've stayed many times in Vieques at another hotel on the Island, but the Inn had a change in ownership, and we wanted to try something different for our return to Vieques for the February get-away. Hix Island House fit the bill.We stayed for ten days in Tiangular House in the Matisse Room. It was fantastic, it was private, our massages were great, the pool was refreshing, and our room was bug free, even though everything is open to the sky! Staff, especially front desk manager Brenda, are the tops. Fresh fruit, juices and baked breads were delivered to our room every day. Weekly cocktail parties at the owners' extraordinary villa gave us a chance to meet the others staying on the compound and hob nob with John Hix and family, the creative inspriation behind Hix Island House.We cooked in the apartment half the time, but got a chance to try out new restaurants on the Island during the rest of the ten days- which was very easy to do since Vieques is such a small island. Our favorite was La Campesena.Vieques is a bit quirky as an island, but what an easy place to get to from the northeast. All in all, the vacation was a value since a 15% discount was offered since we stayed more than a week.Highly recommend if you are interested in something a little different, you want to support an ecco-friendly hotel, and you don't mind being a little isolated from the hum drum of typical resorts.. Jim and Keith

<Author>abhbos
<Content>Concrete Paradise Nestled in the Jungle All I can say is wow! My girlfriend and I just returned from a magical four day stay at Hix. We stayed in the Adobe Loft, which was on the ground floor with a very private patio on which we got massages one afternoon. The trip was one of the most relaxing I have ever had and our stay was a centerpoint for that.The Hix House is actually several different buildings, each with three or four lofts constructed of concrete with unglazed windows. Every loft has some form of private outdoor space and many have outdoor showers. The buildings are designed to interface smoothly with the natural surroundings and as a result there are all manner of plant and (small) animal life around. We frequently saw lizards in our room and there was a set of black hummingbirds hard at work pollinating the trees on our patio. At night, the surroundings are pitch black and the only sounds you hear are insects chirping and the wind rushing through trees. The sky is so clear that you can actually see the Milky Way, a rarity for us city-dwellers.The staff were incredibly helpful and friendly. They made good recommendations for beaches for various purposes (reading books, snorkeling, bodysurfing, etc) and restaurants. They had snorkel equipment for us to borrow and a couple of boogie-boards as well. Every day they would stock the fridge with food to prepare for breakfast: local eggs, fresh baked bread, fresh fruit, jam, butter, milk, coffee, etc. We were also able to supplement this with some fruit from the trees on the grounds.Overall, this was one of the best vacation spots I have ever been to. It is not the place for you if you equate luxury with sterility or people pampering you and scuttling about like servants. However, if you want a beautifully designed (my girlfriend is an architect and she can vouch for this), serene place to spend time on Vieques, this is for you. We can't wait to go back.

<Author>jlpdx
<Content>Wabi-Sabi architecture placed in heavenly setting My wife and I just returned from a nearly 3 week visit to Puerto Rico, the USVI, and St. Marteen. We stayed in many wonderful places, but by far the best was the Hix Island House. We stayed in the Casita ... the architecure was terrific, the setting wonderful and the staff/owners friendly and helpful (and the fresh eggs and bread they brought us each day for breakfast were wonderful). My wife enjoyed the outdoor yoga classes and we both appreciated the quiet setting (its very rural - be prepared that the only sounds you will hear at night are the sounds of the coqi, the crickets and birds, and the roosters in the morning off in the distance). The gracious owners hosted a small cocktail party at their home on the property and we appreciated the chance to meet them and the other guests and learn more about the unique approach to architecture. The island itself was also a treat - we visited three beautiful beaches on the three days we were there and found ouselves on nearly empty white sand beaches with wonderful snorkeling and kayaking. There are several wonderful restaurants within a 5-10 minute drive. I have already recommended the hotel and the island to my friends and co-workers since my return. Dont miss the chance to visit this wonderful Island and when you do include the Hix Island house on your itenerary.

<Author>cdelcor
<Content>De-Stress!!!! If you are looking to get away with your sweetheart ,from the hustle and bustle of the big city, this is the place to go! I went to the Hix Island House for the Christmas and New Year's Holiday with my boyfriend. We absolutley loved it! When we arrived we were pleasantly surprised with our room-lofts as they call them. The cement structure makes each room so neat and clean. And the outside shower is to die for! We expecially liked the homemade bread that was waiting for us in our room along with fresh fruit, juice,eggs, coffee and all the fixings. We were really excited with this feature as we both like to get up and have breakfast in our room before heading out for the day. Our loft was very private and we had a great view of the ocean in the far away horizon. We did not take advantage of the bug nets because there were no bugs at night- but it is there if you need it. I especially enjoyed the pool because it has such a natural flare about it. The pool is not huge but it was just the right size for the amount of guests that were staying there all week. There were no battles for chairs or getting up at 6am to put your towel on a reserved chair. The pool is the perfect place to cool off and read in a quiet setting. The Hix Island house is defintely not your typical all inclusive hotel. It is not a food-factory, or day camp! We actually loved trying out all the restaurants in the downtown area. We even decided to stay in one night because you have the luxury of having a full kitchen so you can cook dinner yourself. We Loved this idea as we dine out all the time living in the city. The grocery stores and convenience stores have tons of things to chose from. I was so relaxed when I left the Hix House! We are planning to go back next year!!!! ....We are still talking about the trip and how we miss hearing all the peepers at night! I highly recommend this hotel to couples or friends who want to get away for a low maitenence vacation! Ladies- leave your heals at home!

<Author>SunL0ver14
<Content>Nice setting, but bedbug central While we had a wonderful time on Vieques, I don't know that I'd stay at Hix again after our experience. Most of the bugs were avoidable by wearing bug spray all the time - it is open air, so this is a necessity - sleeping under the mosquito netting in the room. However, I was eaten alive by bedbugs, which mosquito netting didn't protect against. When I alerted the staff to this fact, their initial reaction was to do all they could to fix it - they sprayed the room extensively, got new sheets etc since they were full that night. We also got a new room the next day, but it was worse. There was no staff reaction when I alerted them to the same problem in a different room. We did enjoy the decor, feel and atmosphere of the place, but without a guarantee of no bedbugs I wouldn't stay there again.

<Author>meliberk
<Content>Luxury camping for too much money! A friend and I stayed here while in Vieques for a wedding. Having read the reviews on Trip Advisor, I was at least forewarned about what kind of experience this would be, but I never expected it to be as extreme as it was.As others have stated here, there are people who love this hotel and the experience they get with it, but for about $300 per night, it is really not for me.The good first, the staff is really wonderful and friendly. The pool was cool and natural, the perfect temperature always without the nasty chlorine that is a part of most hotels. We felt safe on the grounds even though there are no lights to see your way around in the dark.Our room was really no more than a garage. Unfinished concrete walls and floors, no rug, paint or much of any decoration. We actually had a heavy garage door that we had to pull up and down if we wanted to access the patio. There were 2 twin beds that were okay, but not luxurious in any way. We spent the 20 minutes before bed every night fighting all manner of bugs (spiders, mosquitos) and other wildlife (iguanas, lizards). Being that the room was all concrete, any natural sound from outside would reverberate loudly around the room and was deafening while you were trying to sleep.Again, the only saving grace was that I was slightly prepared for this from other reviews, but I hoped for the best. I can definitely appreciate the benefit of an eco-friendly enviornment, but I suggest there also be a benefit of less cost to the consumer if there are going to be no luxuries for luxury prices.

<Content>Hix House......Simply Awesome The Hix House is a perfect way to decompress from your busy, stressful lifestyle. If ever you want to get away from it all, book several days at the Hix House and you won't regret it. Quite honestly, a day or two doesn't quite do it. You really need at least 4 days to appreciate the laid back environment of the complex, the fresh breeze, the beautiful views of the Caribbean off in the distance, and the extremely helpful and friendly staff. Bob Gevinski manages the place in the same laid back, professional style: no stress, no problems, no worries. There isn't a better guy to be running the place. It's a great place to be if you just want to peacefully relax by yourself, read a book, or sit by the beautiful pool. If you get ambitious, the beaches are a 10 minute drive away. And when you're done, you come back and your back in the lap of luxury.But this place is not for everyone. If you want the Hilton or the Hyatt, stay away. It's not like that at all. It's such a different place that you have to see it, and spend time there to really understand the place and what it has to offer.I can't wait to go back again next year when I'll be staying a full week rather than just a few days.

<Author>pastora4
<Content>The good and the bad about vieques This trip to Vieques my friend and I stayed at the Hix Island House, a lover's paradise which is also a B  B. The difference with this B  B is that the guests cook and serve themselves breakfast. The geometrical shapes of the buildings are fascinating and protecting the environment is their mantra. Nestled in the mountains, the terrain is uneven and for the physically fit.Night time provides a heavenly show, I had forgotten about the infinite number of stars and constellations. Driving at night can be scary because of the number of horses and colts on the road. While I was driving, a colt bolted in front of the car and only inches saved us from an accident. The roads are well marked and the people are very friendly and courteous.I would recommend a visit to Vieques and a stay at Hix Island House.

<Author>Hotel_Boy
<Content>A Truly Unique, Amazing Escape! How can you describe the Hix Island House as anything but amazing. For one of the first times in my travels, the hotel lived up to the preconceptions and expectations I had created before my trip. To start, our hosts were Diane, Michael, and Joanne, three of the nicest people on the island as far as I'm concerned. Diane checked us in and led us to our place, Matisse, located in the Triangle House. Along the way, she even picked some fresh lemons and brought them up to the house for us. When you get to your room, there are plenty of windows, but no glass. No Air Con, but an amazing fan. The whole concept of the place is to fit into nature peacefully and disturb it as little as possible. And you honestly get that feel once you set foot in your space. Mosquito nets tastefully hang over the beds (and you're instructed how to use them correctly!), a lovely table with chairs, full kitchen with everything you would need to create your own meals (even some eggs for breakfast and fresh loaves of bread daily!!!), coffee press  beans, etc. The pool area is to die for. Clean water, beautiful views, and many times when you are totally alone! Quite rare at an island resort! I think we even spotted a concrete ping pong table a ways off into the woods. Mr. Hix did an incredible job with the design and execution of his vision. This hotel is NOT for someone looking for a pool boy serving daiquiris, a person with high maintenance needs, or your average tourist. This place is for someone looking to get away and escape. Be alone, without distraction of TV or radios... My point is that you shouldn't stay here if you like staying at a W and having a tub full of pink MM's on arrival. This is for something looking for a bit more out of their trip than extravagance and excess. I never wanted to leave. I look back at the photos and wish I were still there. I have never felt this way about a hotel before. I want to return again and again! The Island of Vieques is unreal. If you are looking for a spot not burdened with tourists and chain restaurants, and to get a real taste of a Caribbean island, then head here for sure! They have some amazing restaurants: Topico is a fabulous seafood joint that was packed with locals. Puerto Rican's have a saying that loosely translates to If it is packed with people, then you can be sure it's good; we also ate at the BBH Hotel. It was modern and elegant, ocean side, and very tasty. It was comparable to a NY City restaurant and was located by the pool of the hotel (the Martini鈥檚 weren鈥檛 so hot!). Many beaches are located down long dirt roads often filled with water holes and mud pits. GET A JEEP! It can be an adventure getting to the beach, but once there the solitude is breath taking. (Don鈥檛 forget to wash your jeep to avoid fees!) At the recommendation of Diane, one of the managers of the Hix House, we went to Blue beach for some snorkeling. She not only described it to a T, but we even found our way out to a deserted coral reef island. There is a beautiful little beach out there. Amazing!I found it very handy to have someone with me that spoke Spanish fluently. But one thing I noticed is that everyone on the island was very friendly and willing to put up with us Gringos who only know one language.

<Author>BoqueronAleph
<Content>Lasting impressions Beauty, harmony, style, minimalist luxury and comfort are truly attainable without compromising, intruding on or perverting nature. This is the message eloquently conveyed to us by the Hix Island House. This was our second visit to this unique place and we can categorically state that, at Hix's, we experience the friendliest coexistence of environment and a man made resting habitat : a serious (not grave!) respect and commitment for a genuine conviviality between human nature creativity and the inherent, constant presence of a natural scenery. Now, you may think: Is this vacation place for purists, poetically inclined, eco-minded people? Well, of course these qualities could enhance the enjoyment of Hix's particular ambiance, but then, the ambiance itself offer the conditions for these sensitivities to arise in you. This means rarely encountering invasive civilization noises or personnel (the on-site, day to day service crew is literally invisible and privacy, as well as silence seems to be of utmost importance for management). Ahhh鈥he blissful, sky open, solar-powered showers鈥he good old majestic breezes interpreted by Australian pines leaves hush or bees buzz鈥?the sumptuous, intimate pool鈥?the undisturbed, window-framed landscape and horizon views鈥?the birds concerts and rain symphonies鈥? Given. People who travel to special locations are conventionally encouraged by the tourism industry to consider amenities. So let's put amenities in proper perspective. At Hix's, amenities are not only plentiful but, above all, thoughtful. For example, you will get an atypically spacious room (only 13 of them) furnished with artful (and useful!) original accessories of world known designers. Thus, if you open up to the aesthetically pleasing surroundings, you are bound to get in touch with your relaxation responses (a short distance to stress decompression) without excluding basic earthy conveniences. Follow me?  Wining and dining has never tasted better (if you look well, in Vieques you can find almost any fine gourmet goods to satisfy a sophisticated palate). And then, you have a very short distance access to some of the most astonishing beaches in the Caribbean to let yourself go. What a treasure! We will definitely return in the future. We want to revisit this small and masterfully designed hotel that serves both: humans seeking to rest in solace embedded in natural beauty and nature itself.

<Author>LaBoricuaCubana
<Content>Absolutely Loved HIX We stayed at Hix Island House for our first trip to Vieques and wedding anniversary. We stayed in Loft 3 which had excellent views and was the perfect size for two people. We loved our private outdoor area and shower. We loved Brenda at the front desk and she even helped us with finding the perfect beaches, restaurants, kayaking trip, and even the flight back to San Juan.Just like the hotel says, it isn't for everyone- I'm not an outdoors type of person but I loved the hotel. Just know to expect some tiny lizards and the expected bugs. Mosquitos were not an issue because of the tradewinds and mosquito netting. We felt totally secluded from the rest of the hotel even though there are no windows. The small kitchen area comes with some basic breakfast goods and home made bread. The rooms also come with all the basics for the beach and even have books and games to borrow. As far as activities in Vieques: We had massages in our room by Kristin which were great and you can not miss the kayaking trip. We've gone to the Bio Bay in Fajardo and the Vieques bay is much brighter. It's not to be missed.We had an excellent dinner at BBH for our anniversary and they gave us a table by the beach. Although the concept was great we were soon eaten by the many mosquitios, minor issue because the food was delicious. I would def. recommend this restaurant. All of the beaches were great except for Green Beach, although the snorkeling was good you can't really lie on the beach for long because of the little gnats that bite incessantly.Vieques is a wondeful vacation destination and we would def. visit them again.

<Author>Chrick
<Content>One of the most romantic place ever I have been traveling for years, and I am always looking for this very special and unique place. Vieques is truly one of the last paradise on earth, and the Hix is the perfect hotel to stay while you are there. From the minute you board the small plane in Fajardo, you will realize that this is a very special place you are going to.The Hix is just adding to this fantastic experience. The concept is fabulous, the design and architectures are like anything else. It is very simplistic, but offers all the services you would expect, including a splendid pool and outside - but private - shower!one word of caution, this may not fit everyone as the lack of windows and the wide door opening are inviting for mosquitoes. Our bed had a mosquito net and they provide with mosquito repellents. There's also no a/c, so it can get a bit hot especially in our unit (Adobe) as it is on the lower floor and there's no as much breeze as the upstairs units.But don't let this stopping you. This is a place like nothing else, and if you want to surprise your wife or husband, I don't think you'll find better.I hope you enjoy the place as much as we did!

<Content>One of Our Best Island Stays One of Our Best Island Stays Ever! Hix Island House was the perfect antidote for the stressful lives we'd been living. We visited in early June and found the lush property to be absolutely beautiful, well maintained and utterly peaceful. From the stunning architecture, to the perfect-sized pool, to the comfortable beds, luxurious linens/robes and the relaxing outdoor shower, everything was so much more than we had hoped for. Even the room amenities were way above (and more thoughtful) than other places we've stayed in the Caribbean. For example, in addition to the usual niceties like aromatic hand soaps and shampoos, our room at Hix also had some surprising and very useful extras: lanterns, bed-side fans, beach chairs/coolers, bug spray and most impressively a well-stocked kitchen. But it was the managers -- Diane and Mike -- that made this vacation one of our best island stays yet. Thanks to their restaurant recommendations and skilled reservation making, we ate extremely well (go to Uva for one of the best island meals you'll ever have) and found gorgeous beaches (Blue Beach for great snorkeling). Without them we would have missed some of the best treasures that Vieques has to offer. We definitely plan to go back!

<Author>pontouf
<Content>needs maintenance to meet price range While we loved Vieques, and appreciated the concept of the Hix Island House, it is in a price range beyond what it offers. Although it is beautiful, the grounds, pool and lofts are in need of maintenance. Many of the dishes in the kitchenette were dirty, and looked like they were 10 years old. Our white towels and robes had stains on them so we asked for new ones and they were very nice about changing them. All of this would be okay if it was slightly cheaper, but it is one of the most expensive places to stay on the island. Additionally, despite the throw on the bed having a colorful pattern, a stain was still visible on it. The concept is peacefulness so there is no maid service, and if you want anything you have to request it at the front desk which is only open between 9 and 5. This is done out of respect for guests tranquility, but then you are paradoxically charged a service charge on your bill in addition to the normal tax. Again, I overall liked the place and the inside/outside design, but at almost $300 a night it's too expensive for what it is.

<Author>shingobingo
<Content>Soak in all that Nature. We just returned from a magnificent five day trip to Vieques. We stayed at the Hix Island House. The room was the 'Adobe Triangular Room'. Even the being on the lower level, showering, watching humming birds dance from lush flower to flower is quite the experience. The windows do not have glass panes, and have wood shutters. it is absolutely raw at its core, so it allows you to engulf the breath-taking surroundings of nature. Echoes of the coqui (the local frog), is absolutely relaxing under the moonlit sky.You can plan all you want, by trying to plan your activities ahead of time. But Brenda at the front desk will gladly help you out with the real deal. She made our trip all the more romantic and exciting with her careful recommendations for dinner, beaches, and the BioBay (which we missed regretfully). Also being a yoga newbie, I couldn't resist taking a class in the morning on the premises. Closing your eyes, breathing and hearing all that nature around you, again...is just amazing. Maybe it's being a city boy, that when I see flowers so rich in color, sounds of birds and coqui, geckos crawling everywhere, and seeing horses in the middle of the road...it's just so exciting.If you want to experience something out of the ordinary, totally relaxed, and absolutely amazing, I highly highly recommend the HIX Island House. The hotel is beautiful, the pool is beautiful, the surroundings are beautiful, and the staff are super friendly. My favorite thing about the HIX is the fresh bread on the kitchen counter, with eggs and fresh fruit in the fridge. Breakfast never tasted so good. Never experienced a vacation as refreshing as this. I will have to do it again soon. An absolute must!

<Author>NyFavabean
<Content>Terrific; not for everyone Hix Island House is absolutely wonderful. It is also not for everyone. Because the hotel rooms are open to the elements, you need to be a bit hardy to enjoy the place. However, if you do have a little bit of an adventuresome spirit, and if your idea of being pampered is something like super luxury car camping, this is the place for you. Having cooking facilities is a big help. And, if you stay at Hix Island House, absolutely positively ask Nilsa to cook you a meal. Simple home cooking: far and away the best food we had on the island! Oh, did I mention the architecture?

<Author>HitoZen
<Content>GREAT if you don't like the crowd, BAD if you love pampered luxury My gf and I just returned from a 3-night stay @ HIH (actually, went 3/12-3/15). Overall, a wonderful experience worthy of many return stays.Considering the positive reviews left by other reviewers, I'll just fill in some blanks on HIH/Vieques that may yet have gone unaddressed by others.* Room. We stayed at the Studio in Casa Triangular, which is where John Hix stayed for more than a decade before HIH was turned into a hotel. Diane/Brenda/Joanne basically said this unit was John's favorite. It must be so considering all the pictures of it featured in the book of John's works (autographed versions sell for $20 at the front desk). Now, contrary to the photos you see on the website (as of 3/13/2006), you do not have a full panorama of waters surrounding Vieques. In the units' line of sight stands a huge Mimosa tree. We were not much disappointed since this tradeoff of view (of easily reachable beaches) vs usability (hammocks that sway with the trade winds now tied to the trees) was a worthwhile one.* Accessibility. As any of the hotel staff would tell you, a car is NECESSARY. You can practically drive to anywhere you'd want to go on the island w/i 15 minutes (aside to/from Green Beach, which was not worth the trip given that its isolation and that we allocated 1 day to beach hop / snorkel). We rented a 2007 PT Cruiser convertible (Touring Edition, 2.4L Turbo) from Martineau Car Rental (almost across from Martinuea Resort; walkable). Now, Martineau was to have us picked up from VQS (which was 5 minutes away from it), yet we waited for 30 minutes only to get to Martineau via publico ($3/p). Martineau was kind enough to throw in a 7% discount on the rental, only to overcharge by 34% when I looked at my cc bill. Lesson here is to make sure to save all your receipts and to be VERY thorough when you do the car inspection upon first receiving the car (take photos if you must; we did but only because we like taking photos of everything).If you're a planner like me, you probably tried (and failed) looking for driving maps for Vieques destinations. Turned out HIH front desk will give you the only good and useful driving map of Vieques. There is no need to waste time finding good maps of Vieques online (and MS Streets and Trips '07, iGuidance 3.0, or Garmin City Navigator US v8 won't have anything good either). All you really need is just the one map that Brenda/Joanne will gladly give you. Now, if you want to plan a bit using the computer nonetheless, use wayhoo.com to get the GPS coordinates of some of the locales and enter them into MSST. Unfortunately, we forgot to get the coords for HIH so can't help you there. Nevertheless, everything is accessible enough that this level of planning is not necessary. You will not get lost easily while on Vieques.* Amenities. The unit came with a well stocked fridge. We had coffee, honey, tea bags, a dozen eggs, 4 mini-cans of Lotus brand OJ and 4 mini-cans of pineapple juice, a Brita water jug, and a good assortment of fruits. We drove to the nearby Green Market and bought cheese and ham to make omelettes in the morning. What would have been great is if HIH stocked Coqui Fire hot sauce (locally made; [--]) in the units, as Green Market was all out of it when we went. FYI, you can try many of the flavors at Belly Buttons at Esperanza waterfront, however. Neither Island Steakhouse nor Chez Shack had any. Lastly, the room also came with lotsa books in case you forgot to bring some, as well as a chess set, scrabble, candle-lit lanterns, and bug spray!* Activities. We spent what equated to 2 days in Vieques. In my mind, this was the appropriate amount if you also plan to visit the main island (which we did for 3 days). Having days starting at 8AM (sun rises at 6:45AM) and ending by sundown @ 7PM, this was our trip allocation: * One full day for beach exploration / snorkel / bum. See 'Beaches' for details.  * Half day for Abe's all-in-one biobay/kayak/snorkel tour. See Abe's' for details. * Half day bumming @ HIH * Quarter day driving around getting to know Vieques. See 'Accessibility' above for details.* Abe's Biobay. [--] There's quite a few options from which to choose for bioluminescent bay tour. We picked Abe's because they were the only one to offer an all-in-one option, combining kayaking, snorkeling, mangrove traversing, and biobay swim. A good deal at $90/person, we met at Belly Buttons @ 1PM, stopped by Green Market to get more beverages, and headed off driving to Mosquito Bay to start our kayak trip across the bay into the mangroves. Kayak across the bay was pretty exhausting but definitely worth it if you don't want to just lounge your days away. Be sure to try some mangrove oysters - very salty but delicious. Abe will chuck them for you. After the mangrove tour, we continued to kayak to Novillo Beach - the secluded beach accessible only by kayak. It was there that we snorkeled for about 1.5 hours. Beach dinner by the sunset was large coldcut subs prepared by Belly Buttons with chips and Caprisun. Be sure to feed the 'pet fish' as they're used to being fed around 6:30PM and will follow you wherever you go. We then headed off in the dark back to the bay where we witnessed the truly amazing dinoflagellates sparkle like little diamonds at night. This is one of those experiences that no digicam can ever capture.* Food / restaurants. We cooked our own breakfast everyday during our stay. A little mouse also joined us one morning and it scurried across the unit. No wonder the wonderful homemade bread was stored in a tupperware. For dinner, we dined at Chez Shack for its Monday BBQ grill night with live music ($35/person after-tax, for entree + beer + AYCE salad bar). Be sure to call in advance to reserve seats, though we'd actually recommend Island Steakhouse AYCE BBQ dinner ($35/person after-tax, for pina colada + AYCE entree). Island's tasted better, did not have overly loud music or slow service, and was not as shacky feeling. (Island's menu consisted of honey corn bread, pulled pork, chicken, baby back ribs, jalape帽o mashed potatoes, and corn on the cob).* Wireless internet. You can either use the iMac at the front desk (that closes at 5PM), or if try to get some weak signals using the 54Mbps wireless connection from the office. Our unit was farthest away from the office unit yet still managed to stream some internet radio with only minor buffering. I hope HIH would spend $50 and get a signal extender. As my gf called it, I suffered from some minor internet withdrawal. * Weather. During the day, temperature remained in the low 80s for the entire trip. Be sure to put on SPF 50 (we only used 15 and 30) since UV gets through cloudy days almost as well as clear days. At night, there was abs no need for AC as the tradewinds really cooled the unit. The gf had the fan off at one point since she got too cold. Only one instance when it rained one night @ 7:30PM for 10 minutes as we rushed to finished building our sand 'castle'. We wished it'd rain a bit more as we did not hear any coqui songs (though we did manage to capture two coquis in the outdoor shower area!)* Beaches. Below is all the information I gathered while searching for beaches. I did not write some of them but figured to save readers time by aggregating what helped us. Favorite was probably Media Luna since that was where I saw a 4ft Mantaray at 4ft of glistening waters. And the sand was fine enough to build detailed sand castles (which we also did, given that my gf's an architect). I've included GPS coords for your convenience.Overview: [--]snorkel: [--]  [--]All the Beaches on Vieques are dependent on the wind direction on any particular day. If the winds are from the Southeast then the North Coast Beaches will be nicer. If the wind is blowing from the Northeast then head for the South Coast Beaches! Pata Prieto (Secret) Beach - VISITED路 Take main Camp Garcia road (sign is small but it'll be the only wide opening you see. If you see many houses then you've driven too far up north)路 Drive for 5 minutes/1.3 miles past Garcia Beach and Playa Caracas (Red Beach) 路 Blue sign says Pata Prieto Beach路 At the Y fork, take right.路 A total of 3 families were there while we were there 10AM - 12:30PM.路 For snorkel: on the FAR left side, follow the rocks around and ~100 feet from the edge. there are rock outcroppings there, and the surf can be dangerous. Snorkel here rivalled what we saw at Navillo Beach via Abe's tour.Media Luna (30ft shallow and lined for protection) - VISITED路 18.08940, -65.45570路 Calmest. We saw mantaray!路 Supposed to have the most kids but there was a total of 3 families stretched over a mile or so of sand.Bahia de la Chiva (Blue Beach) - VISITED路 18.11110, -65.38630路 Had the most people (13 groups; mostly non-family)路 The snorkel was not very good as the water was a bit muggy.Red Beach (Bahia Corcho / Playa Caracas) - VISITED路 18.10750, -65.41570 路 Favorite with locals. Gets crowded.路 I think we stayed all of 4 minutes here because there was too much dried up sea grass.Sun Bay - VISITED路 18.09690, -65.46040Navio Beach路 18.09750 , -65.43880路 Most Turquoise, the widest white sand and often the most deserted路 Only beach with waves (but not good for body surfing)Cayo de Afuera路 For snorkel: South and West/right/ocean are best路 Need to swim/kayak here路 Manatees, nurse sharks, and antler coral!Playa Negrita (black sand)路 Head towards La Hueca, which is located on the southwestern part of the island. From Esperanza head west, you will pass Casa Vieja Art Gallery on your left, slow down and start looking for a dirt road path on your left. You will see a big boulder on this dirt road. You will be driving towards the edge of a cliff, find a place to park around there. Grab your camera, your sandals, put on some sunscreen and walk down a walkway on your left. You will just walk and walk around the coast until you find the black sand beach. I was extremely desperate to get there, but do take your time, it is a beautiful walk towards the beach. As I mentioned earlier you will have to work your way around rock walls. The bottom of the beach is rocky and can get slippery so please walk around with care.Playa Esperanza (for snorkeling)路 Right in front of Trade Winds Guesthouse路 Very easy access for snorkeling Green Beach (for seclusion  snorkel)路 Take the road all the way to the end where it Ts and then go left (it's a pretty rough road)路 Go all the way to the last cut out that leads to the beach. 路 Walk to your right about 90 ~ 120 ft then go in the water (too much sharp coral and sea porcupines in front of the cut out).路 Once in the water swim out about 120 ~ 180 ft and swim to your left. There's a great reef out there and I've seen everything you can see in the water out there: all the fish, turtles, sting rays, manta rays, lobsters, and once a fairly big nurse shark (a couple of years ago).路 Need to leave by 4PM to avoid midges 路 Great drive to get there, have to pass Kiani Lagoon mangroves

<Author>emdawg
<Content>We'll be back This posting can't possibly express my esteem and admiration for what the folks at Hix Island House have put together, but I'll do my best. First off, it is georgeous. The architecture and layout of the place syncs with the stunning natural beauty of Vieques in a way that somehow suggests harmony over and above the obvious luxury. We'll be going back--I don't think we could stay away even if we wanted to.Regarding the service, I'll say this: If you want to feel completely alone, and not be bothered for any reason whatsoever, they'll accomodate you. However, if you need them for anything, they will be there in spades. We unwittingly booked a room on the busiest weekend of the year and couldn't find a rental car or a scooter or even a bike to get around the island. When we realized this might be a problem, we simply called them and I know they tried to track one down for us every day the week prior to our arrival and had pulled off the impossible by the time we landed.When it came time for us to leave the evening of Easter Sunday, a Hix cartaker came to our door two hours before we were to depart and told us our cab driver was getting soused on the beach and wasn't coming. So they drove us to the airport and refused payment!The folks at Hix don't seem to be about taking your money, though I know they're running a business. Instead, it seems that the quality of your experince, of your vacation, is what matters to them. Like I said, we can't wait to go back.

<Author>cortado
<Content>Priviledge of Access Rather Than Amenities = A Mixed Bag Hix Island House is a destination unto itself. If you're willing to pay for the priviledge of access rather than service or amenities, Hix Island House delivers. The architecture and setting are spare and soothing: one experiences a sense of spaciousness there, inpart because the lofts are so much bigger than any hotel room. My partner and I stayed at the Hix Island House for one week and while we enjoyed our visit--the staff is warm, the setting spectacular-- I think it would have been better if I had known the following:While the linens and the prices charged are high-end, the food provided is basic: Letty is a lovely woman and the bread she bakes is good, not great; the juice was canned; the butter was in pre-packaged pats; the jam was from Smucker's; the milk is Parmalat. Add coffee and fruit to this and that is the sum of what you get. So pack your own treats if you're into having a bigger or better selection than what's offered. (We bought greens and muesli from the healthfood store and milk and other groceries from the large grocery store in Isabel Segunda.)Fancier foods --goat cheese, crackers, fiji water, etc... are available at Hix Island House, at the reception desk, for a typically steep hotel-mini-bar price. I would suggest to the management that this stash of food be offered to guests free of charge. It sounds generous, but I think it's only fair, considering the provisions are quite basic. All the restaurants that we were sent to: Chez Shack, Richard's Cafe, Trade Winds, Mama Sanga's -- sucked.Bright Side: We enjoyed the pool and highly recommend the daily yoga lessons with Jennifer. I would also suggest staying in a loft on the 2nd floor or higher; you'll get more light. Vieques itself is a magical place. The people are proud and friendly. Wild horses roam the island and sometimes it seems there are more horses than people. Visit the bioluminescent bay: it's a wonder. The best beach is Red Beach, but make sure you wear sandals: there are prickers in the sand. It's a nice drive out to Green Beach, but it's better for snorkeling than swimming.The best food is at the road-side stands that are open near Sun Bay beach and in the parking lot in downtown Esperanza on Thursdays-Sundays. Chez shack is fine on grill night, but not worth it otherwise. Go to El Quenepo in Esperanza, it is the best of the high-end restaurants. The best restaurant for creole food is at Shaunaa's in Isabel Segunda.

<Author>diana333
<Content>Great Architecture / Different Experience The hotel is much what other reviewers described. The staff is incredibly friendly and helpful with reservations. We missed our flight out to Vieques due to our own stupidity (did not realize about the time difference and failed to change our watches to local time). Both the hotel and rental car company (Island) were very helpful since they both close at 5pm and we were arriving at 5:30. Island Rental Car delivered our car to the hotel and our car key and hotel key were left in an envelope on the door of the reception area. Our room was stocked with fruit, eggs, bread and other great food. I was hoping that the fruit would be a little more local but for the most part it was fruit that I could have bought at home with the stickers on them (plums, apples, pears, oranges, and lemons). There were not very many bugs, which I think is a seasonal thing. I don't think that I could go to this hotel during the wet, buggy season. The outdoor shower was wonderful.For the most part my husband and I felt like we spent a lot of money to go high class camping. We had to be cautious of turning on lights for too long because we didn't want to attract bugs, and I had to read by candlelight under the mosquito net. Our mosquito net could have used a bit of maintenance. There were holes the size of my fist and others the size of my head that would definitely not keep out bugs. I had to try to strategically cover these up, which became a science. There are also adorable lizards living in the rooms, but don't worry they are great. They eat many of the bugs! Another house guest that you will have are mice. We had at least one mouse living in our stove who would come out at night to eat everything. He took a bite of all of the pieces of fruit in the fruit bowl and ate some candy that I had in a plastic bag on my night table. On our last day we heard a lady above us screaming because she found a mouse in her purse. I guess that is nature for you.The pool was nice and warm. A few of the bulbs were out, which made it a little difficult for night swimming, but overall it was nice to have and generally there were no people at the pool when I was in it. The restaurants around the island are really pricey and not really worth the money. We went to Chez Shak (right down the street from the hotel and highly recommended by hotel staff) and I must say that it was WAY OVERPRICED for what we got. The food was good, but we left starving because the portions were so small. My husband and I had two sodas (we don't drink) and swordfish for me and another fish dish for him. The bill came to about $80 including tip, which for the amount of food we got (tiny thin piece of fish and a little squash) is too expensive. We also ate at Tradewinds (decent), Duffy's for lunch (expensive and owned by the same people as Chez Shak, but okay) and M Bar (expensive and not recommended, my fish was overcooked). Overall, the best food that we had was at an authentic Puerto Rican small restaurant on the side of the road. It was reasonably priced and not the same old food that every other restaurant was serving at high prices.For the beaches, we went to Sun Bay (public beach) - very nice calm beach and can park right at the sand edge, Navio Beach - our favorite because the waves were great fun to play in but a lot of seaweed, Red Beach - small beach with shack like cabanas that fill up early but provide nice shade, Secret Beach - small secluded beach, fun to watch the crabs walking along the sand and Green Beach - rocky beach good for snorkeling only. Hopefully this helps give you some ideas about the hotel and island. The architechture is worth seeing because it is impressive and the breezes are nice. Other hotels on the island are also expensive, so it may be worth it to you to spend a little extra and stay at Hix for the experience. In the end, I must say that I was a little relieved to get back to my own house and bed without mice and bugs to worry about.

<Author>paraisodemonteverde
<Content>Wonderful Concept, But Could Be Even Better Hix is as wonderful as others have said from an architectural and concept standpoint -- assuming you like the concept, which we did (just got back). The rooms are fun, interesting, breezy, huge and just feel good to be in. They could use a bit more color and maybe a throw rug to break up the concrete look, but this is a minor criticism. Be sure to get a second-story room; the views are good (although not spectacular) and the feeling is wonderful.The staff was very helpful. We, like all guests who are there on Wednesdays, were treated to a lovely cocktail party at John Hix's own house on the grounds -- a nice touch. Hix was interesting to talk to. The fresh bread was great, and the fruit, eggs, etc. for breakfast were plentiful.We wished there was better landscaping, both around the buildings and at the pool (which was, nevertheless, very nice). Also, the reception building and attached manager's unit isn't Hix's best work, and the area right around the hotel is nothing to look at.Everyone wonders about bug problems at night in the rooms; we found that there were few mosquitoes, but just enough to use the mosquito netting. Problem solved.A wonderful experience (that's what it is; not just a hotel), but for the money, we expected a little bit more in the way of non-architectural, non-service features.

<Author>Groodle
<Content>Fantastic I have never written a review of anything before, but I had such a fantastic stay at this hotel, I felt compelled. It was just a truly excellent experience: The lush grounds and Zen-like rooms were beyond gorgeous, and the managers (and all the people at the front desk) were extremely helpful. This is the type of place that appeals to specific tastes. In other words, it's not for everyone--you are left alone, there is no TV, maid service is only every few days, there is no bar or restaurant, you take out your own trash, and the rooms are open to the outside, allowing lizards and insects free reign. Still, if you're after a peaceful place, with a great bed, an exhilarating outdoor shower, a well-stocked fridge, a gorgeous view, and lots of privacy, Hix is for you. I just returned a few days ago, but I am already dreaming of returning.

<Author>2fromMass
<Content>Can't say enough... I can't say enough to express how incredible my visit to the Hix Island House was. My girlfriend, and I visited the hotel as part of a two-week trip around the Caribbean (other highlights to follow). Vieques and Hix Island House were certainly the crown jewel of our trip! We highly, highly recommend this special place鈥攏ot only because of the stunning architecture (created by owner/architect John Hix) and the spectacular hilltop setting, but also because of the superb hospitality provided by resident managers Mike and Diane and their staff.When we were searching for accommodations in Vieques, we were intrigued by the architecture and open air configuration of the hotel, as beautifully presented on their website. I'll admit we had some reservations about the open air experience (bugs, etc.), but when I called the hotel to inquire about availability, co-manager Diane quickly put our concerns to rest when she explained that their are no dangerous bugs and that the beds are protected with mosquito nets. That was a relief! In addition to booking my room, she was also extremely helpful in explaining flight (we ended up taking Cape Air from San Juan International) and SUV rental options and provided me with their cell phone number in case we had any problems in our travels. I took her up on the offer before I even arrived at the hotel. Despite their clear directions, we managed to take a wrong turn on our way to the hotel. Mike, patiently helped us figure out where we were (near the island's main village, Isabella) and guided us to the hotel.Upon arrival, we fell in love with the architecture. I've never been anywhere like it before. The hotel's three main guest buildings (the aptly named Casa Redona, Casa Triangular, and Casa Rectangular) are even more stunning than they appear in the pictures. While we expected to be awed by the architecture, we had underestimated the serenity and natural beauty of the setting. Hix carefully situated the buildings into the hillside in such a way that each provides its handful of units with privacy, yet each are only steps away from the pool, check-in building, and yoga platform. The subtle, yet well maintained landscaping is the icing on the cake.I concur with previous revierws' accolades. The managers and staff鈥攚hile providing all of the personal service we could ask for (and we did)鈥攚ere never intrusive. In fact, the personal attention was a key reason that our brief visit to Vieques was packed with fond memories. Not only did they guide us to several great meals at the island's restaurants, they told us who to ask for at each one. Of particularly note was nearby Chez Shack鈥攚hich we, following Diane's recommendation, we reached via a spectacular moonlit walk. The restaurant's friendly staff (yes, it is a shack, but with one of the island's top chefs), were particularly attentive when we told them that the Hix House had sent us. Mike helped us with our reservation to explore bioluminescent Mosquito Bay (a Vieques-must-do) and directions to many of the island's secluded beaches鈥攊ncluding our favorite, Blue Beach. The staff was consistently friendly and all seemed to genuinely enjoy their work. JoAnne was a wealth of information about the island.A final note鈥he managers' 3-year old standard poodle, Porter, was a particular joy for my girlfriend, as he reminded her of her childhood dog. He reminded us why we went to the Carribean in the first place鈥o play! We will definitely return.

<Author>Adeliamisskitty
<Content>On a scale of 1 - 10: 11 My husband and I stayed at the Hix Island house, La Casita, for 5 nights during Thanksgiving weekend which includes our anniversary. It was the best vacation we've ever had. The following items contributed:1. The architecture. The concrete building material, the design (high ceilings, clean lines) greatly contributed to our feeling of well-being. It was like being at the newly renovated Museum of Modern Art in New York - no matter where you were in the unit, the visual impact was perfect. The bathroom and outdoor shower area was a dream. The space always looked great no matter how cluttered it got when we left clothes on the ledge and chairs and shoes (sometimes muddy) on the floor. The space is good for your mind.2. The comfort. The bed was great and bed linens wonderful as were the towels, robes and beach blankets. We loved Neeva Gayle's big shirts (and bought 2 black ones to bring home with us. I'm wearing mine right now). The kitchen was designed and appointed extremely well - well enough that we cooked all our breakfasts and 3 out of 5 dinners there (and sat under the stars on our patio and ate them with chilled bottles of Chilean red wine). We made sandwiches with the wonderful freshly baked bread for lunch (we grilled it first, it was good cold-grilled) and took them to the beach a couple of times together with some of the generous amounts of fruit that they provide (upon request). We also used the great beach chairs one day and sat at Sun Bay Beach for 3 hours. 3. The environment. It was, indeed, very romantic. You felt like you were one with nature and we often just sat outdoors on our ocean view patio quietly listening to the sounds and breathing the beautiful, jasmine scented air. The only time of day when it was too hot and bright to be on the patio was during lunch and then we would bring the small dining table and chairs indoors, close to the door opening, and have our lunch in the cool bunker-like indoor environment, with the door wide open. The shower, as I mentioned, was heavenly with a full ocean view and a wide ledge where you could place your cooling drink (i.e. a late afternoon beer) while you showered. The pool was divine - very low in chemicals and beautifully designed. I was there early every morning for my exercise and there was never anybody else there. We also took a wonderful, romantic evening swim one night under the stars (pool is open until 11pm).4. Very importantly: the people who own the place and the staff who work there. John Hix, the architect, is a genious (sorry to embarrass you John). His wife Neeva Gayle, is also a genious. They are absolutely great, caring, people and we feel like our lives are richer for having met them. In my opinion the item service includes the philosophy behind the place and my husband and I love the philosophy behind the Hix Island House: nature can't be controlled and the best way to enjoy nature on your vacation is to be close to it, not sealed off from it. Here you are close to it in a beautiful, comfortable environment.All the people we met who worked there: Diane, Brenda, Joan, were absolutely wonderful and helped us with everything we asked for - made reservations, replenished our room, gave us directions. As far as the replenishing is concerned, that's what made it such a great value for us because we got as much fruit and bread as we asked for and that accounts for a large part of our diet (we brought our own oats for oatmeal in the morning). They also provide eggs, milk, jelly, juices and even olive oil that we used for cooking. We made fried rice one night with the eggs. The lemons that grow on the property are wonderful to put in your cold water or beer. To everybody who hates bugs - I have researched the issue plus I know from my sister's experience from 20 years in Puerto Rico that there are no killer bugs in the Caribbean. Even scorpions and tarantulas are harmless. Remember, we are a FAR greater danger to them and their environment than they are to us. They may cause skin irritations but that's about all. I always bring Lanacain or something to sooth bug bites. We should all just enjoy every last little creature 'cause who knows how long we'll all be around at the rate that we humans are destroying our shared environment. All those little creatures are part of the chain - they all serve a purpose. Why can't we ever get that into our heads? The last Caribbean vacation we took last February our cottage was full of bugs and we just reminded ourselves of that and felt very calm about it.To sum it up: we intend to go back to the Hix Island House as much as we can and we would like to try all of the units eventually.

<Author>RItraveller
<Content>Romantic 25th anniversary at Hix! Just returned from 3 nights at HIH and we could not have had a better experience. We only wished that we could have stayed longer. We were celebrating our 25th wedding anniversary and found HIH to be a sensual, romantic experience in every way.Everything starts with the design of the rooms and grounds. Our room (Loft 1) was designed so that the natural world was always present. Whether it was the sun reflecting off the brushed concrete wall in the morning or the fabulous night sky viewed from our outdoor shower, we were never far from nature. The rooms are designed to take advantage of prevailing breezes to cool the room so that there is no need for air-conditioning. This allows you to hear the coqui at night, the birds in the morning or the breeze rustling through the leaves in the tree outside the bedroom window. Yes there are occasional insects, but we used the candle powered lanterns and mosquito netting at night and had absolutely no problems.The amenities in the room were perfect. The kitchen was well equipped and we could have easily entertained several guests. We made breakfast in our kitchen each morning which saved time and money. The homemade brown nut bread was delicious toasted on the griddle. The bed was comfortable with plenty of pillows and the swinging bed on the deck was a nice touch. The grounds are beautiful, but not in a manicured formal garden sort of way. There are at least two trees with small lemons which can be used in drinks, etc. The pool uses a filtration system that minimizes the use of chemicals. The water is clean, warm and relaxing as you float under the palms. We arrived after 5PM on a Friday and there was no one else around so we had the pool to ourselves. It was a great way to unwind after a long day of traveling. Swimming at night under a sky with a million stars was magical. The staff (Michael, Diane, Brenda and Joanne) was friendly and helpful. They provided recommendations answered questions (the biobay trip is an incredible experience which should not be missed) and but did not intrude on our solitude. The masseuse they recommended (Lee) was excellent. Honor system beers and cold drinks at the front desk were a nice convenience.  Despite our enthusiasm, I agree with other reviews in that HIH isn鈥檛 for everyone. You are exposed to nature in ways that just don鈥檛 exist at most other hotels. If you are open to a different but wonderful experience, be prepared for one of the most romantic experiences of your life.

<Author>godessathena
<Content>Unforgettable and wonderful August 16-18, 2006 My husband and I spent 2 days and nights at Hix Island house while on our honeymoon and it was unforgettable! We stayed in La Casita and had a million dollar view. The room was great. The outdoor shower was great. How do you describe an experience that goes beyond words? Ever so often, you could smell the scent of wild jasmine floating in the air. It didn't matter whether is was during the day or night the scent was just suddenly there. All day long the birds serenade you and at dusk the tree frogs take over. We laughed at the 5 minute overlap of the two which just sounds like 'noise'!! No place else did I hear the sounds of nature and smell the scent of jasmine like I did from our room. The temperature, even in August was always perfect. We laid on the lounge chairs in the morning and evening and watched all the different little birds flit around. We never saw another guest while we were there. We cruised around in the jeep exploring, snorkled, played, and enjoyed the beautiful little island and then returned happily to our room. We prepared most of our meals there and ate on the little patio and enjoyed our view. After spending 2 days on Flamenco Beach on Culebra I was in need of a massage which Hix booked for me in my room. They arranged for us to take the BioBay kayak tour which is a 'must-see' if you go to Vieques. When it came time to leave our jeep wouldn't start. So to make sure that we didn't miss our flight out they drove us to the airport and also called the car company to let them know where the car was. They took care of everything for us! Hix Island House is the most memorable place that I have ever stayed and we most definitely plan to return someday. It is unequalled and exceeded my expectations! Thank you Hix for such a memorable stay!

<Author>missmaggie
<Content>Not Very Service Oriented The architecture and property site are quite unique, however I think the price is too high for what you get.The front desk is only open from 8 to 5 (unless the managers decide to close early for the day). If you need anything when the office is closed, you call a manager on their cell phone and wait.If you need additional supplies after the first day (shampoo, soap, etc), you need to stop by the front desk and request it.Daily maid service is provided at an extra charge, so if you make coffee and breakfast in the morning, be prepared to clean up quick or the bugs get to it.The rooms are starting to get a bit run down; there is mold in the outdoor shower, rust stains in and on the refrigerator, the fan was out of balance and squeaked all night and there were missing light bulbs.Also keep in mind, while there is visual privacy in most of the units, the openness results in little sound privacy.All in all, I think for my $245/night, I am looking for a bit more of a service-oriented hotel versus one that just relies on a it's architectural appeal.
