<Author>paulieg19
<Content>Hix = Vieques. Tranquility. I signed up on TripAdvisor specifically to give a favorable review of the experience my wife  I had at Hix (we stayed in early March - I'm a slacker...).My wife and I were at our mental limits and had to get away, but I demanded some place different because I travel frequently for my job so I've grown numb to 5-star hotels/resorts, which all look  feel the same to me. I just wanted peace  quiet, away from people being paid to be nice to me. My wife, on the other hand, freely admits she likes to be pampered on vacations; but she compromised for this trip because I was particularly burnt out. Surprisingly, she was absolutely blown away by Hix. Not surprisingly, so was I.Recalling the trip afterwards, we agreed that one of the most memorable moments (along with BioBay, the great food downtown, having the Vieques beaches all to ourselves) was our initial shock opening the door to our room. It was huge, and beautiful in its minimalism. There was one reviewer who used the word sterile - wrong. Minimalist is a genuine compliment, as the Hix perfectly melds with the overall experience of Vieques. This is an island with only 10k people owning just 40% of the land; the electricity still occasionally goes out - for the whole island. Hix lets you quietly melt into the background and fully experience the tranquility of Vieques.Our view was gorgeous. An obligatory photo of the outdoor shower. Our room was huge. The bread  fruit was tasty, and the fridge a great option. And the outdoor yoga was by far the best yoga I've ever had; fresh air, rising sun, day heating up (good for flexibility).I highly recommend going to the Green Store for lunch picnics and grabbing the occasional breakfast or dinner materials. We went to another store and found worms in our pancake mix. We also swatted some small gnats at night when we played Scrabble (they have several board games downstairs). These things do not ruin a trip; they're part of the experience of an island that miraculously remains one of the best kept travel secrets. The best part of the trip was the lack of TV, computer, or any other electronic/media distraction. We tore thru books, we had a blast  a few fights playing Scrabble, and we had the unusual experience of just being with each other with no distractions. If that sounds boring, don't go to Vieques or Hix. If you want to go to an island for a fake getaway with self-important people dressed in $100 'casual' shorts - go to Nantucket. If you want to relax unencumbered with your loved one on the most unique vacation you two will take, fly or boat to Vieques and stay at Hix. It was our favorite getaway yet (and we travel *a lot*), and wouldn't have been the same if we hadn't stayed at Hix.

<Author>cpmt
<Content>Pay attention to your instincts While planning our honeymoon in Vieques, I insisted that at least two nights be spent at Hix Island House. It seemed perfect for us鈥攖ranquility, privacy, nature, and beautiful design. The first afternoon was great. Brenda was helpful and quickly made reservations for dinner at Chez Shack and a bio bay tour the next day. We spent a few hours lounging by the pool after the beach and then had wine, cheese and crackers in our 鈥渞oom鈥?(the studio). Lizards sunned themselves on our balcony and birds flew in and out. It was very peaceful and unlike anything we鈥檇 ever done before. However, the night changed everything. It would have been too dark and steep to walk back from nearby Chez Shack, so we had to drive. Bugs flitted around us as we played scrabble by candlelight. It rained on and off and was very hot, despite the overhead fan. I tossed and turned and only slept a few hours for fear of disturbing the mosquito net and getting eaten alive while we slept. The next morning we tried to make French toast with the homemade bread, while fighting off a combination of mosquitos, flies, rain, and powerful wind. (I鈥檓 sure this would have been easier had it not been the rainy season.)I felt guilty admitting to my husband that I hadn鈥檛 done enough soul searching and that Hix wasn鈥檛 what I had expected. Luckily, he was sweet enough to make everything okay. He talked to the ladies at the reception desk and they were sympathetic. They refunded us 75% of the second night鈥檚 stay and we checked into Hacienda Tamarindo鈥攁 place that isn鈥檛 stylish or cool, but our room had an amazing view of the ocean, private balcony and the option of keeping out most of the bugs.Although it was an interesting experience being at Hix, I wouldn鈥檛 call it romantic, because it was very difficult to relax. Although I did love camping as a kid, it wasn鈥檛 the right experience for our honeymoon. I know there are MANY others out there who love Hix and I鈥檓 not trying to contradict them鈥攕imply giving our take. I hope this helps those out there planning similar trips!

<Author>skatterbraind
<Content>Back in Chicago . . . and homesick for Hix The descriptions posted by other travelers of this hotel are pretty spot-on, for the most part. The design is stunning, the views are incredible, and the staff is so attentive to your needs.My wife (we just got married down in Vieques, and had our reception at the Casona) and I can't pay enough compliments to the managers, Diane and Michael, and our personal answer girl, Brenda. We've never felt choked up about checking out of a hotel, but this time, it was like saying goodbye to old friends . . . these three were our family in Vieques, and we're really going to miss them. Brenda, always cheerful, always helpful, will get you sorted on what to do and where to go when you're on this beautifully sleepy little island. In the weeks leading up to our trip, she was my point of contact for making sure everything was in order. On top of that, she helped serve food at our reception (more on that later), and our guests paid compliment after compliment on how much they loved Brenda. Michael saved our reception from dissolving into an evening of sit and stare. Unfortunately, a few of our 'party' guests dropped out at the last second, and we were left with an unhealthy mix of old and young that was hesitant to sit back and enjoy themselves. Mike played DJ for a bit and had the salsa going, and although people still refused to dance (my feet hurt/I'm tired/etc), Mike and Diane were dancing, and eventually a limbo stick popped out, and I ended up in the pool in my wedding pants. More people followed (some forcibly) and the mood loosened after that. ---- On a side note, while I didn't get a chance to try any, Mike won a hot sauce competition this past weekend, so be sure to ask him for a taste . . . I've gotta ask him to send us a bottle . . . As for Diane . . . working with Brenda, she made the entire trip as seamless as possible; she made sure we had chicken for the dinner the night before the wedding, she got the flowers to us in time for the ceremony, she softened the blows of 'wedding planning disasters' I encountered -- we could not have pulled off this wedding without her. It's rather rare to meet someone who's a genuinely kind person -- who's not just smiling because she has to. We feel fortunate to have had the opportunity to meet her and this Hix family. The hotel itself is astounding. We were lucky enough to rent out the whole hotel for our wedding guests, so we got to experience each of the lofts. Thunderstorms in your room, coqui (tree frogs native to PR) on your kitchen counter, lizards on your patio furniture, outdoor showers -- all very, very cool. The view from the 'skydeck' of Matisse, I believe (top of Casa Triangular), is beyond words. I'd never seen the Milky Way outside of pictures and the occasional trip to the Adler Planetarium here in Chicago -- on a clear night, the stars are right there with you. If you're worried about mosquitos, yes, you'll get a few bites, but so did couples that were staying in typical Inns and resorts on the island. Honestly, we got more mosquito bites eating at Island Steakhouse (awesome food!) than we did from eating in our loft. Put on some spray and you'll be fine. We had a bit of . . . uh . . . 'naked time,' and the bugs respected our privacy.I'd recommend staying in one of the upper lofts; we stayed in Loft 1 and loved it, but again, we were able to check out the other lofts as well since our guests were basically in every room. The upper lofts were nicer than the lower lofts if only because they had better views. For the love of God, though, if you're squeamish about bugs or lizards or creatures that go 'coqui' in the night, stay at Martineau Bay or something. The reviews that have been posted thus far are accurate, for the most part (admittedly, I was a little nervous about reading nothing but glowing reviews, and paid more attention to the negative than the positive comments). The person complaining about not getting bread -- there's a food request sheet at the front desk, we got everything we wanted every time we requested it. Write what you want down before 1:00 or something, and you'll get it, simple as that. We had zero problems in that regard. Sorry about the rambling nature of this review; we're still in a bit of a whirlwind from everything. While in Vieques, check out Sun Bay, Blue Beach, Red Beach, go snorkeling off Mosquito Pier and check out some starfish, eat at Island Steakhouse and Tradewinds, have a drink at Inn on the Blue Horizon, feed the horses around Hix some mangos, watch a sunset at the gringo bar in Isabelle Segunda (something Mar, I can't remember), say hey to Owen from Casa de Amistad (really cool guy), stop in for a chat with Tom at Tom's Flowers in Esperanza (also a really nice guy, did our flowers and went through hell trying to make it back from his vacation, kinduva funny story), and send Brenda, Michael (ask for some music recommendations), and Diane regards from Bernadette and Mike -- a couple of newlyweds enchanted by our experience in Vieques. We'll most definitely be back, if only just to say hello to some of the nicest people we've met in a very long time.Oh! And stay away from Martineau Car Rental if you can! Our Jeep sucked!

<Author>bdogmama
<Content>Grain of salt.. Yes, believe the reviews...Hix is all that, and more. But be realistic about your expectations. There are no windows and you are exposed. I was shocked to find out that I thought Hix was a little too one with nature for my comfort level (I thought I would be down with the bugs and rain) but in actuality found it much more camping than luxury hotel. Don't get me wrong, it is architecturally striking, environmentally friendly and a retreat from technology and the mundane routine. But it's not for everyone (and i'm not exactly a princess type). It just didn't live up to it's expectations once I arrived...and we didn't get daily fresh baked bread...we got one for the week. The owners were nice...enough...but not overly so (we met them once). I guess we'd heard all the hype about how wonderful Hix was and were a little disappointed it didn't live up to it.Something about being surrounded by concrete was rather disconcerting, almost sterile. The view was okay, we thought we would have a view of the ocean from our room. The furniture is actually very patio furniture like (in fairness the accessories were unique and wonderful), they have to be durable because yes, it will rain in your living room (and it makes the concrete slippery). We arrived in the beginning of rainy season and the bugs were bad - very bad. But my husband never got bitten. Our mosquito net told a story in the morning...I was afraid to do yoga - something about the combo of deet, sweat and bugs - which I had really been looking forward to as part of our trip. Turns out it was cancelled frequently anyway. The lizards are a novelty in the beginning but we grew tired of them all over our kitchen along with other friends with 4 and 8 legs.Bugs aside...If you're traveling to Hix, here are my suggestions:Bring books for the daytime, maybe even your computer (I know, I know...) for the DVD player with some movies for the evening.Split up your time (if you have it) to really experience the different flavors of the island - the areas are very different (Isabella, Bravo Beach, Esperanza) and Hix is somewhat isolated in more of a hilltop area. Good for privacy and solitude, not if you want to be closer to the action (restaurants, beaches, etc...especially at night). There are many beautiful places to stay on the island.Check out as many restaurants as you can!Of course I don't want to make it seem horrible. All of the things other writers have mentioned - I loved the oversized nightshirts, they provided books and games and the shower was hot. But for the price you pay it's not a luxury hotel as much as an eco-B  B or camping for architect buffs...

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fabulous stay I recently stayed with a few friends at the Hix Island House over Memorial Day weekend, and must emphatically say that it was one of the best vacations I have ever had. If you are turned off, as I am, by the crowded, souvenir-shop infested, overpriced, commercial tourist traps that so much of the Caribbean has become, then you will love the unspoiled, natural beauty of this island and the elegant simplicity of this hotel.It takes about a day to fully appreciate the genius of the inn's architecture; when I first walked into my room I didn't quite get the huge open-air window cutouts and the polished concrete that makes up the countertops, floors, and walls of the buildings. However, the rooms are designed so that the gentle breeze is constant, eliminating the need for air conditioning, and it seemed almost miraculous that concrete could feel so comfortable and rooms so completely open to the outdoors could be so private (because of the way the buildings are situated on the slope.) And nothing feels better than taking an open-air (but totally private) shower. We stayed in a room called the Studio, and it had a nice kitchen stocked with fresh bread, coffee, juice, milk, and everything we needed, so we didn't need to leave our room until we were ready to go exploring. I spent long mornings reading on our terrace, listening to the birds singing and the wild horses neighing. The beaches were postcard beautiful and nearly deserted, even the public beach with its restrooms and concession (which served surprisingly good food). If you like driving around, there are many dirt roads leading to remote coastal areas. We also had lunch and dinner in the two tiny towns, Isabel Segundo and Esperanza, and the food was excellent wherever we went. The highlight of the weekend was the nighttime kayaking trip to Mosquito Bay (there were no mosquitos at all), which is said to be the greatest example of bioluminescence (millions of tiny organisms that light up when disturbed, or splashed) in the world. It absolutely has to be experienced to be believed. Just kicking in the water makes it light up like a fountain.Though the setting at Hix Island House is very private, the entire staff is very approachable and works hard to make guests feel comfortable. I would definitely stay there again.  
<Date>Jun 19, 2006

<Author>unwind
<Content>Entering the 'Zone'.... and I'm not talking about the Zone Diet, which is hopeless with the wonderful homemade bread served each day. I'm refering to unwinding and relaxing to recharge you batteries.I got to this state in about half a day at Hix Island house, a record on any vacation. Innkeepers Mike and Dianne made sure we knew where to go, what to do, and where to eat. Their friendly, relaxed attitude will get you the full lowdown on the island and all it has to offer. The thing is.... it's OK if you don't step a foot out of Hix, enjoy the pool, take a walk, lounge out in the tropical setting and feel the gentle breeze of the Carribean. But what about the BUGS!? It's the tropics and you've got a non-airconditioned room open to the elements. We'll the breeze took care of the air-conditioning part. It was incredibly rejuvenating not to be in a hotel with the air-conditioning pumping away all night.The bugs were on vacation. I don't know if it's the breeze, or the dry season but they didn't pose a problem. I came fully prepared to douse myself with chemicals but in the end the cans of spray stayed on the shelf. Ok so where's the bad part? I hate reading reviews where people just keep gushing on and on, you know there must be something they're not telling you. We'll first if you rent a vehicle, make sure it's a high clearance Jeep like car. A quick shower can turn the roadsinto large puddles (if you asked Mike and Dianne they would have told you about this). It's fun if you have a Jeep but not so great if you get stuck in you Neon. Next even if you have a Jeep it's not a great idea to go exploring on a path in the jungle that no one has been down in the last 10 years. It might just... end and then you've got an interesting multi-point turn (speaking from experience). Also the scratches on the vehicle might be a problem when you return it to the rent-a-car place (errr... what scratches?) Last, Mike and Dianne will tell you about all the nice restaurants on the island. It's surprising how many there are.You should go visit every one of them if you get into your zone running or exercising. If you got into you zone lounging then don't be surprised about the extra bagage you're carrying on your way back.Last, don't miss the bio-bay on a moonless night, it's an out of this world experience!

<Author>Albatross37
<Content>Starbeds at The Hix Last month we had our wedding at The Hix House. During that time we spent 7 nights there, and had the whole place rented out for three nights during the wedding so that many of our friends and family (dogs included) could stay there. Having paid a visit on a scoping mission in October 鈥?5 we compared the Hix to both the Inn on the Blue Horizon, and Hacienda Tamarindo. We decided on the Hix because it is the complete package, having stunning views, exceptionally helpful managers in Diane and Michael, and a secluded privacy. As well, offering unique rooms of varied design, which take advantage of being in the tropics by being open walled, with many having outdoor showers. Additionally if your lifestyle makes you an environmentally conscious person, the Hix House is designed with a value system that is ecologically aware making your choice a responsible one as well.We enjoyed all the Hix had to offer, quite moments with nature, sweeping vistas from many of the rooms, a wonderful pool, and helpful staff that never let any communicated need go unattended.Based on having experienced all the rooms there I would highly recommend two over all others, 鈥淭he Studio鈥?and 鈥淟oft 1鈥? both offer the best of the Hix experience. While there we ate at Chez Shack, which is just a quick walk down the road and worth a repeat visit on a night that is not Bar-b-que night. Zee Foods, an Organic store a little further down the road is also a good place to get prepared meals that you can store in your Fridge at The Hix and have as a mid-day snack during a break from the pool, or take to the beach. A place to avoid is the restaurant at The Inn on the Blue Horizon.For weddings the setting could not be better. The staff facilitated our every need. Nature provided a perfect backdrop. When we go back I know exactly where we will stay, what else can you say!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Simplicity with just the right amount of help HIH was great. I appreciated everything about this hotel. The rooms are spectacular -- outside shower (but private), sparse and clean furnishings, great bread and food in the fridge, nightshirts made from egyptian cotton, high quality towels and linens. The kitchen had everything we needed to make dinner and used the Zee Store and the Green Store down the road to supplement what they gave us in the room. The grounds are beautiful, not manicured to give a natural feel. The environmentally friendly practices made us feel better about burning all that jet fuel on the way to and from Boston. Take a few Yoga classes and GET A MASSAGE FROM CHRISTINE! I had 2 and they were fabulous! Listening to the wind in the palms outside our room during a generously long massage was heavenly. Brenda at the front desk was so accomodating, she made suggestions and reservations for us the entire week. She is great. We enjoyed the food at Medina Luna the most, but the fun ambiance of Chez Shack on Reagee night was cool. It was also nice to be able to walk to dinner. Tapas at BBH was also very good. But of course the beaches were the best way to spend the day. We went to all the beaches on the way out to Blue beach and enjoyed the all for different reasons. Some were wavy and good for body surfing. Others were easy to swim and fun to snorkle. The one regret we had was that we didn't go to Green Beach with snorkling equiptment. We waited until the last day to go there and found it to be the best beach for potential cool fish sightings. Lots of nice boats to look at from mainland PR. Some people told us not to tell anyone about beautiful Vieques, but we are spreading the word. I am sure the local people and businesses would appreciate the tourists. I just hope the island finds a way to maintain its natural beauty and not become another all inclusive haven. Vieques is too special for that. Go, relax and enjoy a wonderful hotel and island.

<Author>beachloverGlenRock
<Content>Hix is a Bit of Heaven We just returned from a wonderful relaxing week at THE HIX ISLAND HOUSE on Vieques, Puerto Rico. We had read about the resort in the NYTIMES and were facinated by the ecology-minded ideas that went into the planning of this peaceful place. The three guest buildings do indeed blend into the land. They are built with large open areas which face the east. As you rest in your bed, you are bathed in moonlight at night and sunlight by day. The showers are placed so that the run-off waters the beautiful natural foliage of the property. The spacious interiors are simple and clean, and equipped with comfortable furniture and the loveliest of linens. Much of the furniture is handmade by John Hix!We were greeted by Diane, Brenda and Michael. They welcomed us with great warmth and gave us the low-down on all the nice places to eat and interesting things to do. Brenda made reservations for us immediately at the popular restaurants and the Biobay.We enjoyed our week immensely. The weather was perfect. We visited many beaches and did some wonderful snorkeling. The local food was delicious and innovative. The visit to Biobay and the swim with the tiny sparkling plankton was an experience we will never forget. There was not time in a week to see all we wanted to see so we will be back next February!

<Author>ChelseaNY
<Content>Unbelieveable The website for this place doesn't begin to show how cool it is. I can see why people say it's not for everyone, but it was perfect for us. If you can appreciate modern, sort of minimalist design, then you will love it. It's all concrete, yet totally comfortable. The fact that it's open to the elements isn't as much of a factor as I would have thought. There were a few lizards on the walls, but we loved them! The open window was incredible - see the attached photo of our sunset view.The loft was absolutely huge and beautiful. You don't have the usual hotel amenities, but it was great having a fully-equipped kitchen, because we got tired of going to mediocre but expensive restaurants. (Tropical Baby was good but suffered from a gross burned oil smell; Media Luna was good but just not great for the money.)It didn't bother us at all being a few miles from the beach. No matter where you stay, you have to drive to the good beaches anyway. We loved Red Beach, even though it was a bit more crowded - great waves for bodysurfing. Blue Beach and Navio were nice, too. Didn't make it to Green Beach, but we did snorkel with Abe at Mosquito Pier, and saw a barracuda! A note about rental cars - I wouldn't rent from Marco's again. We had a very frustrating experience trying to switch cars when ours wasn't working. We went back there five times and he was never open - during regular business hours. I think there must be more reputable places.After staying at Hix, I can't imagine staying anywhere else on Vieques.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>REVIEWS ARE ACCURATE My girlfriend and I just returned from Vieques, where we stayed at Hix for three nights. Having now stayed there, I went back and re-read all the reviews on here, and I would say they are generally accurate.For the few who found it a negative experience, I think that more than anything it was just a mis-match. Yes - it is very open. If the idea of the occasional moth flying near your head gets you all worked-up, HIX IS NOT THE PLACE FOR YOU! Go somewhere with screens and windows - you'll be a lot happier. It is also about a 10 minute drive from either of the main towns (where all the restaurants are located) and about 15 from most of the beaches - so if you're not going to rent a car, or you want to roll out of ben onto the beach, again, HIX IS NOT THE PLACE FOR YOU.All that being said - I will now tell you why we give this place 5 stars (or circles...as the case is). As has already been said, the setting is STUNNING. Beatifully maintained grounds - and yet you wonder if it all just grows that way (it doesn't - but they keep it very eu naturale). Tropical flowers of countless varieties EVERYWHERE. Mango trees. Noni trees. Birds of paradaise. Magnolia trees. You name it - if it grows in the tropics, it's probably on the grounds at Hix. There are humming-birds EVERYWHERE - zipping from flower to flower, doing their thing. Just amazing to watch.The rooms are ALL fantastic. We were lucky enough to have Consuelo show us EVERY ONE (there happened to be nobody there when we arrived, and we virtually had the pick of the place). Each has it's selling-point, and I think their website does a good job of showcasing all the rooms. We decided to sacrifice the outdoor shower (for one with a large window, which we figured was almost as good) and we stayed in Matisse - which has its own roof-top view, complete with a beautiful flowering cactus garden. We probably would have taken Loft 1, but alas, it was the ONLY one that was reserved for the time we were there. I can't say we cared. I think we would have been happy in any of them (honestly - we saw them ALL). Each has a nice bathroom with plenty of towels, and a FULL kitchen stocked with pots, pans, knives, dishes etc. The also stock the room each day with fresh baked bread (baked by the staff), eggs, butter, corn-flakes, milk, juice, tea, jams, lots of fruit (ALL delicious and fresh). We were also doing backflips to find a coffee grinder, french press and whole beans, but found the coffe to be pretty bad. After buying some fresh in town, which was WORSE than what was given to us by Hix, we figured that was as good as it gets in Vieques. On the other hand, we are total coffee-snobs, and will probably bring our own next time. There are also some nice perks in the rooms (chess board, books, beautiful local art) which will make you feel more at home during your stay.The staff is great. Very accomodating and eager to please, but for the most part stays out of your way unless you need something. There is an honor bar at the reception area filled with nice cheeses, soda, and water - which you can help yourself to for a minimal fee. We were hitting the thing a LOT, and only paid about $25 for everything we took - which we thought was more than fair (i.e. not mini-bar prices). The weather we had was a mix of blistering sun, partial clouds, and down-pouring rain. We were happy to see it all. The rain (and darkness) brought the most amazing chorus of tree-frogs. There was the occasional mosqueto, but no more than you would get anywhere in the tropics. We found the light breeze that was blowing kept them moving. I would also recommend using ONLY CANDLE LIGHT at night (they supply TONS of tealights, lanterns, lighter etc - another nice touch) as this will keep many of the bugs that are attracted to light away from your room. They also put in the room plenty of Off and Raid - neither of which we touched. The bed has a mosqueto net draped over it, which you should use. We found it to also be very romantic - regardless of whether it was needed.We ate out two of the nights at restaurants recommended by Consuelo and found them very good (but VERY expensive!). We are from NYC and eat out a LOT, and even we found the prices a bit over-the-top. But the food was very good, so we just laughed at how incongruent it was with the rest of the island's rustic, minimalistic feel. It's only money, right?The Bio-bay tour was one of the most amazing things I have ever seen. Water that literally GLOWS when you move it - and glows BRIGHTLY. I will never forget seeing fish darting underwater, leaving a trail of glowing water behind them. It also poured with rain while we were out there, which was INCREDIBLE - each raindrop that hit GLOWED. You have to see this to believe it - and to go to Vieques without seeing it would be like going to Egypt and not seeing the pyramids! All in all, we had a wonderful stay at Hix. The island of Vieques was great for us. We enjoyed the undeveloped, rustic style - and the occasional wild horse running in front of our car as we sped around the narrow roads. The beaches we hit (Red, Blue, Sun Bay, Bahia de la Chiva, Navio and Media Luna) were all different, but nice. Some were rougher (good for body surfing) and some were very calm with sugary sand (good for being a slug). We found the snorkeling to be average for the most part, but did find some coral and beautiful fish off the east coast of the island at Bahia de la Chiva.If we could make one change with Hix, it would be that to have them come in the room each day and straighten-up and give fresh towels. The towels were given to us with a smile upon asking, and keeping in stride with their theme of environmentally friendly - I guess it's to be expected. This was not a problem or anything - just something we thought.We have traveled a LOT in the Caribbean, and I would say this was one of the nicest placed we have been to. Not nice in the way that you're pampered, but nice in the way that you can appreciate a beautiful, tropical setting from a cleverly designed, open air loft apartment - with all the comforts of home right in your room. It was perfect for us, and we will definitely return. We have so many positive memories of our short time there.Sorry this was so long, but I hope it helps. Have fun, where ever you go (GO TO HIX!).

<Author>madam_bomb
<Content>Camping in style Hix House is great. The resort is set atop the hill with the buildings facing east/west. This gives you great morning views for most of the lower buildings, although the higher original building I think has better sunset views. The pool is beautiful and the lack of chlorine is refreshing. The birds and lizards around are great natural interest. The large amount of roosters on the island can be annoying (they don't just crow at dawn).The service was helpful, setting up tours and restaurant reservations. The island is definitely for outdoorsy people who don't just want to shop and plop and as you must drive, you'll have to be used to narrow winding, sometimes rough roads. The snorkeling was great especially around the island at Blue Beach and the rocks off of Green Beach (which isn't a relaxing beach, it's more for snorkeling or swimming). And the bio-bay is just mind-blowing. Take the Kayak tour with Abe. He's great.As far as restaurants go: La Sirena is a joke of bad management and despite the good tamales it's only worth getting a beer or watching the theatre of the owner fighting with her help. Bili is quite good but a little pricey for what it is. The Tiki Hut sandwich shop is good for breakfast but the sandwiches are a bit strange (the owner was very nice and let us get food just before he closed). Bananas had such bad taste in music (Britney Spears, etc.), it seemed it was only for the culturally challenged. Uvas in Isabel is by far the best hands down despite the price; service, food and the patio setting (don't eat inside it's nice but the patio is great). Michaels deli at Bravo! isn't worth the trip, just average and overpriced for the effort and what's up with the gourmet deli business plan? Why not a real restaurant? And finally, the highlight, Tropical Baby in Isabel. Great brunch and apparently a good dinner. If you're looking for a good supermarket to buy food for the room . . . good luck, we couldn't find it. People kept pointing us to it, but as far as we could tell we were either lost or there really wasn't a supermarket.We were in loft five and the only drawback was the sun streaming in at dawn. If you're an early riser (unlike myself) then you'd love this loft.Overall Vieques is a great place to visit, resembling a typical Mexican town (or rather two towns Isabel II and Esperanza) and offers great outdoor fun.

<Author>nospeel
<Content>Amazing Relaxation! We just returned from an amazing week at the Hix Island House. Vieques is an amazing island. It is not for those that do not want to work a little. You need to do a little searching and driving for the beaches (over bumpy unpaved roads). And, all other activities - kayaking, snorkeling, hiking, exploring take a similar amount of effort. But, if you are, like us, somewhat adventuresome, your effort is well rewarded.The Hix Island House is THE place to stay on the island. It is like sleeping in a fabulous - well designed outdoor shelter - with the amenities of a upscale hotel. Chris and Kurt are amazing hosts. Morning yoga with Jennifer is a great way to start the day. And, Consuela helps cater to your every whim.Sleeping in the perfectly warm tradewinds (which keep away the bugs) with the sounds of nature in your ears and millions of stars in your eyes is a true delight. Waking to the morning sun and preparing breakfast with the amazing nut bread baked by Curt is the perfect way to start your day.Be prepared for having to make a very tough decision every day... Which of the many incredible beaches will you visit - life does not get much better than this!

<Author>090909
<Content>Heavenly Oasis We stayed at Hix Island House in late February 2005 for 4 nights. What an enchanting place. John Hix has created a strikingly natural setting for the 13 open-air loft apartments. Each day we feel asleep and awoke to the sounds of nature. The outdoor showers are fantastic (and private), as is the crystal clear pool.If you're considering staying at Hix, understand that this is a place intended for quiet. You can hear your neighbor if he or she is speaking in a booming voice or making noise. That's the whole point of coming to Hix Island House - to slow down, find quiet and solitude, and be aware of your natural surroundings. Don't come here if you want to play loud music, party or behave as though no one can hear.Kurt and Christianna are very welcoming hosts, as is the office manager, Consuelo. The HIH resident mini pinscher, Apollo, will melt your heart. He is the nicest, friendliest dog who pretends to love every guest the most (Apollo must be the most photographed dog on the island).Although HIH is not located directly on the beach, it was never an issue. As long as you have a Jeep (don't rent a sedan - a 4-wheel drive is a must), you can be at totally secluded beaches in a short 10 minutes. There are great beaches throughout the island and on many you will never see another person. Our favorite was Navio for the waves and Red Beach for the calm, gentle waters.Best restaurant on the island: Chez Shack, which is just up the road from Hix Island House (walking distance). Their fresh seafood is by far the best on the island.

<Content>a once in a lifetime experience My husband and I had never been to Vieques before, so everything was very new to us. Hix Island House is beautiful, just like what you see in the pictures. It is a completely different experience than anything else we have ever done................as we guessed it would be. We actually split our vacation between it and another property just to try different things. (and to be completely honest we weren't sure about the no a/c thing...........to be even more honest, we brought a small box fan with us just in case-a little embaressing, I know)The outdoor shower is incredible, and very private.............as are the rooms even though they are so open to the outdoors. (water pressure and temparature was wonderful) Also, some of the rooms have a floating bed type contraption that hangs from the ceiling that you can lie on and read, star gaze, nap, etc. and we put it to good use during our stay. Everything about Hix Island House is relaxing. Most of our stay it was raining in Vieques, but we still had a magnificent time. The views are breathtaking, and you just feel one with the nature that surrounds you. Having time with your loved one with no interruptions is priceless! (No t.v., no phone, no computer)One last thing that makes Hix special is Kurt and Christianna. They were so helpful with rides into town to get our rental car to dinner recommendations, etc. One night they recommended Media Luna for dinner and we ended up seeing them there when we had finished eating. Our taxi was running a little behind, so they offered to take us back to HIH. They are so kind.If you want a once in a lifetime experience in a beautiful, tranquil setting where you can totally relax HIH is the place!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>You Want To Relax? Hix Island House! Hix Island House is terrific. It is a unique eco-resort that is probably unlike any place you have ever stayed. It is a place where you are immersed in nature (on the fantastic island of Vieques) and can truly relax: no phones, televisions, radios, clocks. You wake up to the sounds of birds and fall asleep to the sounds of tree frogs. But Hix Island House isn't for everyone. If you want a standard resort with air-conditioning, maid-service, and a bar that serves fruity drinks then you should look elsewhere. That is not what Hix Island House is about.When I read the occasional clunker of a review I realize that the folks writing those reviews didn't do their homework. Complaining about the lack of windows or air-conditioning?! That's the whole point of this place as the Hix Island House website clearly states. The rooms you stay in are made entirely of concrete and each room has a wall missing. So you don't get a/c. But what you get in return is the opportunity to watch the sun rise and the moon rise from your bed and listen to all the sounds of nature without any break between you and the world around you. Yes, some rain will get into your room if it rains but you will not get wet. And it is wonderful to be lulled to sleep by the sound of a rainstorm.Here's the neat things about this place: A refrigerator stocked with fresh coffee, eggs, juice and cereal. Eating breakfast with your sweetie looking down to the ocean and watching the hummingbirds flit from flower to flower. Comfy bed linens, towels and robes. Taking a shower that is both private and exposed so that you can look over the landscape. Chatting with the terrific managers Christianna and Kurt. Swimming in a gorgeous pool in the evening and hearing nothing but frogs and crickets. Wandering the grounds and seeing not another soul. No phone. No tv. No radio. No clocks. Total relaxation.If that sounds good to you stay here. If you can't live without glass windows and an air conditioner look elsewhere.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hated it!! It is like camping but very expensive! Hix Island House was not for us!!! This is no luxury place. It was like camping, yes it was relaxing, but the relaxation stops at night. If it rains you hear every drop, and it feels very closed-in because the windows are actually wood shutters. There is no glass so you can't look out. I find it hard to believe that all these people were so happy with this place, just being honest, hope this helps!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Best Web Date Ever We now live in Philadelphia but I grew up in P.R. and left when I was 18. My wife, never having been, was in need of some real relaxation. I decided to look at Vieques and happened upon Hix Island House on line. W/O anything else, I threw caution to the wind, and after five minutes, decided to book an entire week and thus, call it a blind web date. We stayed at Casa Redondo in loft 3. WOW! And that is coming from a guy who has been to ALL the islands between Cuba and S.A. Yup, there are bugs, it is the tropics, and there is no T.V., Phone or room service. Yet, it is pure magic. My wife who is bug phobic had no problem whatsoever. It is like staying in a modern tree house set up for the Jetsons meet eco-life. Very modern and yet natural. No silly closed windows with AC blaring. Yet, it is too nice to explain. The hosts were amazing. For the first time, ever, my wife relaxed 200%. We didn't run to see stuff, we didn't cram stuff in, we simply relaxed. The pool is enough to make you apply for a job there. Rent a car, go to the beach, lay around in the room, shower in your private outdoor shower, pick mangos off the dozens of trees, laugh at the wild tame horses, dogs, cats and lizards. Watch the clouds roll past the windows. Take in the amazing fauna. Bring two good books. We found ourselves going to bed at 9 or 10 and waking up at 7 like rested babies. Eat at the Viequen for breakfast and dinner at M. Lastly, the people on that island are the most helpful and kindest you will ever find. Just don't rush! The hosts, Kurt  Christianna, were always there to help and just made the trip perfect. There seems to be some confusion as to who is writing these reviews. Just to keep it real you can email me with questions. I can't rave enough about the quality of this place.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Exotic but not luxurious I have to agree with the first review that staying at the HIH is ALOT like camping. If you do not enjoy being outside, need air conditioning or hate bugs, you will most likely not be comfortable there. We went in the off season, so it was very wet - nothing ever dried out completely. We stayed at HIH for 3 nights, which was enough - although we're very glad to have experienced it and will do so again in the future.The grounds and architecture are minimally invasive (very hidden) and fabulous. It's not manicured landscaping like you would find over at the Wyndam, but what would be there naturally. Beautiful. The pool area is stunning, and the water feels very clean (low chemical pool). Although we stayed on the top floor of Casa Rectangular during a booked memorial day weekend (according to innkeepers) we rarely saw or heard another person. The open floorplan gave views of the coast over the tree tops, and the nights were amazingly starry and peaceful. That same open floorplan lets the sun come glaring in EARLY (5:30 - 6 am) - so if you like to sleep late on vacation it's going to be difficult.There is no maid service, but whenever you request something it's there. The coffee is good, the bread somewhat tasty but a little mushy (maybe its the rainy season again). Nothing on Vieques is local (ie: fruit), so expect your basic apple and orange combo flown in from mainland PR.As for the luxury linens/furniture - we had a couple of Frette towels and I think the bedspread was from Ikea. We could care less what kind of linens are provided (again this was not luxury), or furniture - but if it's advertised as such then people expect it to be so. Also we had one very uncomfortable lounge chair made from plywood and a broken plastic armchair - so to sit together we had to perch on the balcony.The innkeepers (Kurt and Christianne) are helpful and very interesting to talk with. Being from over-developed Florida we appreciate what John Hix has created - an attempt to be minimally invasive and environmentally conscious. Overall we would stay at HIH again not expecting luxury, but expecting a quiet, relaxing experience.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Like camping - only better First of all, if you don't like to camp, you won't like Hix Island House. The rooms are open which means: no lights after dark and no leaving food lying around. I love camping so I didn't have any problems. In fact, it's better because you didn't have to worry about the tents collapsing and you have a constant supply of hot water. :) I just got back from my trip and I miss Hix already. The frogs, called coquis (co-keys), will serenade you to sleep. The rains will lull you into peacefulness. The sun and the roosters will signal the new day. The views are breath-taking. The pool divine.I never once wished for a TV, AC, or DVD. (not included in the room) I brought my own radio/alarm clock. (No clocks in room either.) The room also doesn't have a phone but there is one phone at the main office.I went in off-season, so this may not be true all year around. The island pretty much shuts down at 9 - 10. Bars don't stay open late and there's no place to dance and congregate. Vieques is an island to get away from it all. Don't expect coffee shops, ice cream stands, or bookstores. I found two chains - Directv and the USPS. If that isn't your cup of tea and you need your TV, DVD, AM/FM, then maybe Hix isn't the place for you.Being a single female traveler, I never once felt threatened during my stay at Hix, Vieques, or San Juan.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Space to Remember John Hix and Neevagayle have created both an architectural wonder and a welcoming oasis on a Caribbean island that embodies all that we love about the Caribbean: aquamarine blue waters, powder sand beaches, open spaces untainted by overdevelopment, creative Caribbean influenced cuisine and beautiful weather. It is hard to put into words the way in which Hix has integrated his finished and polished concrete structures into the landscape, but it echoes Japanese tea houses where distinctions between inside and outside no longer apply. Stay in the Matisse room, you'll never think about your physical living space the same again. Mark and Guadalupe

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Unique and Relaxing Vacation Our stay at Hix Island House was one of the most relaxing vacations I have been on. I had done my homework and knew quite a bit about the resort before I arrived. However, for me, it exceeded my expectations!This is a beautiful place high in the hills.Beautiful tradewinds meant very few bugs while we were there - I only got one mosquito bite during my entire stay in Vieques. Our room was large and spacious and wonderful. It was as open as they described - we had a large patio that was completely open to the outside (there is a metal grate if that makes you more comfortable at night) A ceiling fan made our nights comfortable and we never ever noticed the lack of air conditioning. The openness of our room (missing the fourth wall as we were on the ground floor) made it completely unnecessary. At the same time we were never cold either. The kitchen contained all the utensils, plates and things we required (paper towel, etc). Neeva's potato bread is excellent and was still warm and wrapped in a linen towel when we arrived. A fruit bowl was also inviting when we checked in. We love to cook and it was wonderful to have a spacious area to prepare our own snacks and meals. Grocery shops are just a short drive away. The reception desk and hostesses were incredibly helpful with restaurant recommendations, directions, bookings, everything.A yoga class that I did while I was there was just that - a real yoga class where people from outside the place came to practice. Nightimes were incredible - beautiful star watching, especially from the lounge chairs that we had.One reviewer from last year felt the location was not convenient. Everyone is entitled to their own opinion. In my opinion, a car is essential for visiting Vieques. I can't imagine anyone coming to Vieques without one. We rented a Honda Element and found we were close to everything on the island. After a week of driving around from the Hix Island House, our gas bill was $14US. I think the location is central and perfect.Part of our experience was feeling as if the place was our home. And we truly did. We enjoyed washing our own dishes and making our bed. If we needed anything, we simply asked reception and it was done.Vieques was a wonderful place for peace and quiet. Most nights we 'hung out' watching the stars or reading. We had a truly wonderful meal at Cafe Media Luna one night - the tasting menu is fantastic. Another highly regarded restaurant Chez Shack is just at the end of the street (walking distance)I will definitely be back!  
<Date>Mar 1, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>It is like a dream.... We have never experienced such a relaxing holiday as our few days at Hix Island House and the wonderful little island of Vieques. Vieques was a refreshing change from the other Caribbean islands we have visited, in that there was never a lineup experienced, security concerns were rarely if ever present, the beaches were incredible, and the restaurants, surprisingly for such a small place, were of exceptional quality and variety. In response to this setting, John and Neeva Gayle Hix have created the perfect complement. Imagine sleeping in a shell with an 18' wide opening to the softest breezes imaginable at your feet, and waking to the sun gently rising over the Caribbean each morning and illuminating your studio in a warm glow. The achievement of the architecture is that you have a very immediate connection to the natural environment (ocean breezes, sun and shadow, sounds of birds and coqui), yet are protected from the heat of the sun and the night-time rain showers, and can regulate it very easily by manipulating the windowless openings to the exterior. The connection between interior and exterior is often vague - living spaces that project unimpeded to the open sky, showers for each suite that are either open directly to the view or the sky or both, outdoor dining courtyards protected from the wind... The minimal, stongly geometric forms of the buildings magnify the beauty of the natural surroundings and very successfully capture the spirit of the climate. The grounds are a clever combination of wild trees and plants, with shots of colour or form presented by flowering vines and dramatic tall grasses, all orchestrated to provide privacy for the guests and a wonderful ambiance similar to ancient ruins in a jungle. One of the best discoveries is the award-winning swimming pool, with its copper-treated water and view over the hills to the ocean. The hospitality of the owners and staff were excellent, with a very well stocked refrigerator upon arrival, fresh-baked bread (which should be available for export!) and yoga lessons on site, and an eagerness to assure that guests make the most of their stay on the island by readily recommending interesting sites and good restaurants. Hix Island House is definitely a 'design destination', and in conjunction with the interests of its owners in environmental conservation, is also an experience unlike any others we know of. If you enjoy adventure and good design, we highly recommend it.  
<Date>Feb 10, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nature in control....not out of control. John and Neeva Gayle have set the stage for those who seek serenity and calm in the center of Nature's wonders. John's unique architectural style allows you to observe the natural setting without feeling you're the intrusion. The Caribbean winds play with his forms like delicate fingers on a fine string instrument with hummingbirds, King birds and cukoos chiming in as the chorus. Neeva Gayle's refined aesthetic sets the mood in each of the lofts and her homemade breads reinforce the comfort zone. She always makes you feel you're at home and goes the extra mile to make the holiday perfect.One visit to HIH and the unpretentious island of Viequez will reward you with desire to do it again and again.
